$productID.: B001UE6MIO
$rev_NAME.: Vaughn "The answer man!"
$Helpful?.: [946, 965] $review_date.: 08 4, 2009
$REVIEW.: IMPRESSION BASED ON EXPERIENCE:This is my second pair of Motorola 2-Way radios.  I have tried other bands like Midland and been very disappointed, but Motorola has never let me down.  I needed two extra radios for a fishing trip to Colorado so that my father, my brother, my son and I could stay in touch.  I was amazed at how good these radios did in the mountains.  At one point I was over three miles away from my father on the other side of a mountain and we could still talk clearly.  Now I know 3 miles in not as far as the 23 miles range that is claimed these radios can reach, but if you know anything about how these radios transmit, then you know that for it to transmit clearly through 3 miles of solid mountain is close to a miracle.  I have a pair of Midland G-300 Two Way Radios that claim a 10 mild range that cannot even reach 1/2 a mile through forest on straight level ground.  I was also impressed with the battery life.  Even after a long day of heavy use these units had plenty of power left.  One was left on over night after being used all day and it still had power the next day.Since I want this review to be helpful to people people wanting to buy these, I want to make something clear.  The range claim that any 2-way radio manufacturer makes, is base on optimum conditions with no structural or atmospheric interference.  In real life you can never expect to get those kinds of ranges out of any unit.  Due to the curvature of the earth I would not expect that any radio could reach farther then 10 miles under normal conditions unless each radio is located in an elevated position with a valley in between, such as on either side of the Grand Canyon.  So when you buy a 2-way radio, don't pay much attention to the range claims that are made.  Just make sure that they will do what you need them to and don't expect a miracle that deifies the laws of physics.PROS:Motorola quality, great range and battery life.CONS:None that I can find.THE BOTTOM LINE:If you are looking for a good pair of 2-way radios for hiking, camping, fishing or similar, look no farther.  If you are looking for 2-way radios for some sort of specialized professional use or something else these may or may not be what you are looking for.

$review_text.: After using this laptop for a few weeks I have decided to finally review it. Regardless of the negative parts of the laptop if you buy the base model with Dual 755 Nvidia graphic cards it's totally worth it so keep that in mind when I review the laptop. Things I did even before I turned on the laptop was install an SSD hard drive (removed the 1tb with 8gb cache hard drive they do not give you mmc ssd anymore) and  installed 16 gb of OCZ memory (removed the generic memory that came with the laptop)Overall the laptop is very nicely built. My only problem with it is that if you lean your hands on the edge of the laptop while typing the edge is somewhat sharp and bothered me a bit. I am not really sure why they did this they could have easily made is smooth.Keyboard placement and lighting is really good. I like having a 10 key on a 15 inch laptop so it's a really nice feature. Track pad outside of windows is pretty bad (while using acronis to ghost the 1tb hard drive to the SSD)  but once windows boots up it works just like any other touch pad.LCD and Sound worked great didn't have any issues with it at all. Very happy with it. Try and get the Matte LCD not Glossy if you don't want to see your reflection while playing games. I made sure I got the Matte.Wifi... Now this is where the laptop loses a star. The wifi included with the laptop is complete junk. I use a 2.4ghz mouse and it basically made the wifi null. I am not sure why they only included a 2.4ghz N wifi on this model. They could have either put a 2.4/5ghz or even a newer AC wifi card. It only costs around 20-30 dollars to replace this on your own but I left it in to review. I have an old core2duo Lenovo and even it came with a 2.4/5ghz wifi card!Another issue I have is with power mgt on this laptop. What I don't understand is this laptop is a SLI 755 when plugged into the wall which is great and works perfectly with all the game I played on it. However when it's running off battery and switches to using only the GPU on the CPU I don't understand why you only get 3 hours battery life. This slightly confuses me since your not using either 755 video card so why does it use so much juice. I assume it's just because the battery is super tiny and can't hold anymore than 3 hours worth of juice. This doesn't really lose a star since I knew about this ahead of time and I don't plan on using the laptop off the AC anyways. But if someone was buying this for school and gaming I would look at a different brand of laptop for sure.Another feature that makes me mad with Lenono itself and not the laptop is the fact that they said in the advertisements you could get an ultra bay Fan module (yes there is a fan on the video card ultra bay but since that generates a lot of heat it's mute). This was a lie. They never made it for USA customers and I have yet to even find an aftermarket one. It would have been really nice to have one since a lot of the games I play are MMO and I don't need to run SLI to play them but since I can be playing for hours at a time an extra fan built in would be nice for keeping the laptop cool. I have a cool pad for the bottom but as you know that doesn't really cool the internals of the laptop very well.So overall for the price you can't find a better laptop even if you get a cheaper dual 750 I would pick it up. Just make sure you budget to replace the Memory, Hard drive, Wifi if you really want the laptop to scream.

However with headsets perhaps the number one factor has to be comfort is this is where the Tritton is let down horribly.The earpiece is too big (bith with and without the rubber cover) and the ear hook to keep it in place is terrible.  It actually pinches your ear, is not very flexable and is just clipped onto the actual headset so I wouldn't rate it's durability very well either.The recharging base is USB, therefore needs to be plugged into a computer or similar to draw power.  You can't just plug it straight into a wall socket.If Tritton fixed the problem with comfortability then this could be a very good headset, as it is you really can't wear it for long without it hurting therefore my recommendation would be to pass on this.

$REVIEW.: You're likely buying this to connect the mini DisplayPort (or Thunderbolt port) to a monitor with a DisplayPort. I bought this to hook up my iMac to a new 27-inch WQHD display I bought and it works like a charm.Important: Apple isn't great at supporting 3rd party displays. I, at first, thought that there was something wrong with this cable because I kept getting faint display irregularities (faint red pixels on whites). But, no issues on Bootcamp (Windows 8.1). Turns out that while I was getting 2560x1440 support, my monitor was detected as a Television, which can cause all kinds of weird issues. The resolution is to force RGB mode for your monitor, which there are sites out there that'll show you what to do. If you have issues with this cable on OS X, just confirm that your monitor is being detected as a monitor first before assuming it is bad.

We just wanted a small device that we could use to find each other if we got separated while travelling
We didn't want to go the sim card route because the phones may become an expensive target for thieves
At home we can just use our cell phones


I figure in an emergency we could also call for help if we were hiking in a forest or other more remote area where phone reception isn't available

One of the units is a bit louder (speaker and ring) at the lowest setting, but it is acceptable

Unfortunately we found out later that we cannot use these units overseas (Mexico and Canada are fine)
I guess in other parts of the world they use the same frequencies for their emergency services and will confiscate these if you try to bring them in
There are European versions that use different frequencies and are okay for travel in Europe, but you have to purchase those over there

So we may have to do without for now.

$review_text.: Noticed I didn't write mini-router, because in spite of its small size it performs as well as a regular size router, but it has many more capabilities. Some of the most important ones are the following: It's portable, and it comes with a  Lithium 2000mAh chargeable battery, it supports 3G Router Mode, WISP Client Router Mode, Wireless Router Mode, Access Point, Repeater, Bridge with Access Point and Client. It includes a 10/100 RJ45 Ethernet port, and one micro USB port, and it's compatible with iPad, iTouch, Android Phone, Kindle and the majority portable WiFi devices.It also comes with a complete command control panel or web management page that can be access with any browser by typing [...] in the address bar. It can be easy to setup by choosing Quick Setup or if one needs it, it can be set in a custom detailed way using many security features like parental control or WEP, WPA/WPA2, WPA-PSK/WPA2-PSK authentication, and TKIP/AES encryption security. I uploaded a screen shot of the web management page where the many options are displayed.My favorite mode is the WISP Client Router Mode because in this mode, the TL-MR3040 is wirelessly connected to the WISP (Wireless Internet Service Provider) or Access Point and it can share the internet to multiple users. In this instance the TL-MR3040 acts as a wireless adapter, catching the wireless WiFi signal from any Access Point and sharing it. It's my preferred method of using the TL-MR3040, mainly due to the fact that I can plug the TL-MR3040  into the Ethernet port of a laptop or a netbook, leaving the USB ports free to use with other devices while reaching the maximum speed, which in this case is up to 150Mbps - one that excels what the integrated wireless adapter in the device can provide.I got it because I wanted a router that I could use with my Virgin Mobile 3G. The service can be expensive, but at least, I always have a good connection at any time, and anywhere. I added the TL-MR3040  to my emergency kit list because it can be charged like a smartphone, using a solar system charger, or with a car battery using an inverter. This was tested in the most unexpected way after a storm, when we spent a few days without electricity and without our regular Internet connection. I already had the Virgin Mobile 3G for about a year, and it has been useful during previous storms, but during those, I also learned that having a child who is bored and wants to go online, is another issue to deal with during a power outage. So, the TL-MR3040 can be a stress suppressor by allowing to share Internet with the rest of the family at all times.Please keep in mind that like every gadget which uses a Lithium battery, you need to keep charging and discharging the TL-MR3040 battery in order to keep it alive. Using the modem while traveling and storing it after coming home until the next time you need it, might result in a dead battery. So, just use it once in a while around the house. It's a good way to share a connection with friends or family members that are visiting during the weekend, for example.

$REVIEW.: First thing this camera did was make me aware of how much better the image quality of my DSLR is.  I haven't looked at point and shoot pictures with any kind of criticism since last Christmas, and I was originally disappointed with the quality of these pictures.  They tend to be a little noisy/fuzzy, and not necessarily "tack sharp," BUT THEY'RE FROM A POINT AND SHOOT THAT IS WATER PROOF!  I bought this camera because my hubby regularly dumps us over in the canoe on float trips and there is no rational way to excuse taking more than a grand in camera equipment down river when you know it's going into the water sooner or later.  Have already had previous issues with supposed "water tight bags," not GOING there.  So, a waterproof camera became a "must."This camera is great for fun snap shots and at fairly close range.  The zoom makes you feel like you got maybe 40 or 50 feet closer to whatever you were looking at (at least that was how it felt when I went from unzoomed to zoom from my front porch looking towards my barn and arbor - I had gotten across the front yard and was maybe ten feet from the arbor at "full zoom."  Don't expect to hear a blackbird in the tree a hundred yards away and zoom in on this thing and get a "right beside it" style picture.  Not happening, and with the IQ, you're not going to be able to crop out a really interesting bird picture, either.However, if you're canoeing, at the pool, at the beach, etc., and you want a camera that you don't have to have a heart attack about if you set it down on a beach towel and it comes in contact with sand, or if you take it into the water and some gets splashed on it (do NOT take it to a lower depth than recommended or force water at it because that will invalidate the warranty; also read and review manufacturer's instructions regarding the seals and how to clean the camera after it has been exposed to various elements), this camera is for you.  I think I will enjoy it on my next float trip, even though I'll never get the breath-taking shots I would hope for from this.  Maybe one day I'll get some of my DSLR pictures published/sold and be able to afford to look at higher resolution, better waterproof cameras (maybe pigs will fly, too, because if I got that much money I'd be investing it in an f/2.8 zoom lens), but for what I wanted it for and what its capabilities should be, it meets the test very well.  Since I wasn't bowled over and thrilled by the image quality, though, I'm just going to give it four out of five instead of five stars.Oh - on LCD shooting - the screen hasn't given me trouble in any light (unless you're in some kinds of sunglasses, then you kind of have to look underneath them).  Really it is more than bright enough for regular-style shooting.  :)

$review_text.: Dragon touch 9.7 IPS Allwinner A10Update 2/27/13 TabletExpress complete lack of concern for their customers continues by still selling the tablet as the MID970IPS. MID9716W is the new model and there is a firmware image available for it on TabletRoms.UPDATE 2/14/2013: They are still listing this as the MID970IPS but in fact are shipping a different model with slightly different specs. The ROMS for the MID970IPS will not work on the new tablets but we have access to a new ROM on TabletRoms if anybody need one.UPDATE 1/3/2013: There a currently two custom ROMS for the Dragon Touch 9.7 . Tabletroms is the first sight with a link. They fix pretty much all the bugs that are inherent in the stock firmware including Play working correctly.I have had two of these for a couple months now putting it through it's paces before putting out a review. They retail at the $150-$170 mark. Normally I do a first impressions but one issue with the reseller made me hold back a little which I will go into at the end of the review.First the Manufacturers Specs:Operation system: Android 4.0.4 Support HD Flash 11Main IC: A10 (CPU+ GPU+ VPU) Cortex A8 1.2GScreen: 9.7 inches IPS 5 Points Capacitive Touch 16:9. 1024 * 768Storage: 16GBMemory: 1 GBStorage Extend: 128MB-32GB SD/TF SupportWifi: 802.11b/g/nCamera: Dual-Camera, 2.0Mpx Back, 0.3Mpx FrontG-Sensor: All gravity inductionUSB: Dual Min USB (this ias actually incorrect. It is dual Micro USB)Battery: 7800mAhLanguage: English, Spanish, French, German, Italian, Japanese,Polish ,Russian, ChineseOnline entertainment: Support Online video, online TV, online Movie, Online Music, Online Radio.Game: 3D Game can be supported by internal 3d accelerate of hardware. There are more than 200 thousands kind of free software in google marketMusic Playing: MP3,WMA,APE,FLAC,WAV FormatVideo Playing: Formats Support: MKV(H.264 HP),AVI,RM/RMVB, MPEG-1,MPEG-2Video Output: HDMI 720P to 1080P to 2160P full HD output,and Video OutPut(AV OutPut)The tablet comes with the standard USB cable, OTG adapter, and charger. Functioning Play Store installed. Unit charges off of USB as well.Out of the box this is a nice feeling solid tablet. The screen is bright and crisp, touch is very responsive without being over sensitive. It is a very nice looking 9.7 tablet. There are some pics of the tablet and ports below.This has been a really solid tablet. WiFi is strong, battery life is about 5-6hours with WiFi on. Screen brightness is phenomenal at the low setting.Benchmarks are pretty decent. Stock CaffeineMark gives it 5700-6020 and Quadrant scores a solid 2290, which for an Allwinner A10 with no tweaks is pretty good. The system actually comes stock at 1.2GHZ as opposed to the normal 1.0GHZ that most 1.2GHZ advertised run at. o far all is stable. Have not tired overclocking yet, but I know SetCPU and OverClockWidget work on it.Movies and TV shows look awesome. Netflix works. Speaker sound is pretty good. The system seems to not like AC3 audio too much, it plays it but seems to over modulate it. But that is a complaint on a lot of 4.0.4 devices. Definitely better sound than a lot of other mid range tablets I have and have tested. Movies play great through HDMI to both my big screens.Dual Cameras. What can you say for any front facing web cam quality camera? MEH? Looks good video is fine. Now the 2MP rear facing camera. That is a little different story. This seems to be a step up from a lot of the secondary cameras on tablets. While only 2MP it takes really nice pictures, does well in low light, and has an auto focus feature. You can see the reticles finding and adjusting parts of the image when you are taking pictures. Takes very nice 720P video in good light.E-reading is really strong on this tablet, looks pretty good even in sunlight. 9.7 is, IMHO, the perfect size for comic and graphic novel reading.Overall this tablet itself is a great little tablet for the price. If saving a few bucks over the latest and greatest dual core is good for you than this is the tablet for you.But let's get to the issue I mentioned earlier. More and more tablets are being released onto the market with little to no support from the resellers or manufacturers. This used to be almost solely limited to China direct white box tablets. But lately it is becoming more common in US based sellers as well. Zeki is a good example, great tablet, zero support from the manufacturer.In the case of the DragonTouch by Tablets Express, the first unit I got had dust under the digitizer. Customer service from Tablets Express was quick to respond and I had an exchange in a little over a week, on their dime. Pretty cool. The new unit arrived, it was shipped powered on and in sleep mod. Now technically nothing wrong with that except running electronics are more susceptible to thing like moisture, shock when running. When it woke, the tablet froze. When I powered it back on nothing happened. I connected it to my PC and was able to show that the device would boot into fel mode (the hardware recovery) and the Livesuit drivers would install successfully. I contacted Tablet express to see about getting a link to firmware to flash. They wanted me to ship the tablet back to them for testing. I replied that if they gave me a link that I could test for them and save us all time and money, they again stated I could send back the tablet and if it was defective they would replace it. After several attempts to explain to them I was not just a joe schmoe user and I knew what I was doing, even going as far as to offer a non disclosure agreement, I gave in and sent the tablet back. After some more e-mails about future tablet updates a response came that "had no idea how to flash or the firmware for the tablet." Wow. But as far as replacing the tablets they are fast and courteous.This all boils down to, this is a really solid tablet. But if you like to play with and customize your Android firmware, there is currently no stock firmware image to fall back on if your should kill an install. There are scripts available that can pull the necessary files needed to build a Livesuit image to flash, but it is a tedious and not 100% guaranteed process. As with most Allwinner tablets there is not a typical recovery to boot into, but the firmware does say it will run updates from microsd so that could be a way to go.I would give this a 5 out of 5 stars if it wasn't for the firmware not being available. I would still recommend it, unless you are tinker junkie then it all depends on how you look at no established image for recover.

$review_text.: The TRENDnet Wireless N Gaming Adapter TEW-647GA allows you to connect devices with an ethernet plug to a wireless connection on your own wireless network or wireless internet router/modem

 Typically, this is not used for laptops or desktops (for which you would use a USB or other wireless adapter that you can configure from the laptop/desktop)


 Instead it is used to connect "dumb" devices, like some game systems, other hardware, or in my case, a Yamaha CVP-509 digital piano.Because "dumb" devices don't have a way to configure a wireless connection, you first have to set up the TRENDnet Wireless N Gaming Adapter TEW-647GA on your desktop or laptop using the downloadable or CD-ROM based configurator wizard
 A warning to Windows users: when you first run the wizard, some Windows configurations will pop up a warning that asks how you would like the wizard to connect to the network


 If you do not choose the least restrictive option, you will be unable to configure the adapter

 The configurator will lead you through several steps


 The exact series will depend on how you want to connect to your network


 After it has finished configuring the adapter, it will instruct you to unplug the adapter from the desktop or laptop and plug it into the "dumb" device

 If you were successful, your device will now be connected to the internet, so that you can download games or connect to other players online (or, so that you can download music, piano radio, or piano lessons as in my case).I had some problems in getting the configurator to work
 Each time, the configuration failed, without any advice on how to fix it
 Although the TRENDnet support site did not seem to offer any searchable solutions, a Google search indicates that this is a known issue that can be resolved by contacting TRENDnet customer support.

It looks good because it lines up and has a matching batter compartment and slope, but does not give me the advantage I get from laptop trackpads.What I mean is that laptop pointing devices let you keep both hands in typing position while accessing a pointer (joystick or trackpad) with a thumb. So my preference is to take the magic trackpad and put it in front of the keyboard (reversed so the thick part is toward me) rather than beside the keyboard. This almost allows me to keep both hands in one place as I do on the laptop. But unfortunately the slope is wrong. If the trackpad were flat then I could come closer to the laptop experience.As it is the product is not bad. It's no worse than using a mouse, the usual desktop experience of moving your hand from the keyboard to use the pointing device. But in that case I prefer my magic mouse that has both the multi-touch and the mouse that I am just used to while using a desktop.I think Apple made an interesting innovation here and a very good looking product (as usual). I just give it a star short of perfect because I see it as a bit of a gimmick (against my magic mouse) and I think a little more thoughtfulness would have made something closer to the laptop trackpad experience, which I find far more convenient. Maybe in time I will get used to this new tracking device, but so far I have stuck with the magic mouse and the trackpad sits by the wayside looking petty.

$REVIEW.: Ever since Apple's Magic Mouse appeared a few years ago, I had wondered why some entrepreneurial manufacturer hadn't picked up on the idea of a low-profile quality mouse that could also be PC compatible. There have been a few, but in many cases, the emphasis has been on price and not quality.ThisLogitech Ultrathin Touch Mouse T630 for Windows 8 Touch Gesturesis up to the standards of quality that we've seen from this company before with their other mouse products. Will admit that I'm a mouse person, and only use the touchpad when no mouse is available.  This product is not a conventional mouse in the sense that we've been accustomed to, but more on that later. Have spent some weeks living with this new mouse so far, and here my highly-subjective key points found so far, followed with some expanded details.&#9670; Pros:+ Excellent manufacture quality; this mouse is certainly no toy+ Professional looking minimalist design looking; brushed metallic trim+ Small and compact; excellent size for carrying while mobile+ Internal battery powered; USB charger cable included+ Two Bluetooth channels; pairs with multiple devices+ Supports Windows 8 gestures+ Three year warranty&#9670; Cons:- Charging port is on the bottom of the mouse instead of side or end- No included carrying pouch&#9670; On the Fence: Small for larger adults hands; may take some getting used to&#9670; In Use:The packaging is impressive, and immediately one can see that this is a serious product... but for traditional mouse users, it will take some getting used to. The gesture controls from Windows 8/8.1 did not bother me, but it lacks the mouse buttons and scroll wheel to which many of us have been accustomed. The feel in use is good, but it does have a light touch.Had no trouble using this Touch Mouse T630 with either my Windows 8.1 notebook or with my Windows 7 PC, but there's a slightly different feel with each. Its compact size is a bit disarming, as at its broadest points, the T630 measures 3 inches in length, and 2 inches in width. It is a scant  inch in depth, and that tapers down towards the front end.In truth, I did not like the feel of this Touch Mouse T630 at first, and set it aside in frustration after the first few minutes. But in fairness, and feeling that this would be the trend in future mouse products, went back to it, and slowly am warming to its use.  It is still better than using the native touchpad in a notebook.&#9670; Summary:TheLogitech Ultrathin Touch Mouse T630is a well engineered product that looks and feels good. It recharges quickly, taking about a minute, which will give you power to keep going for 45 to 60 minutes. Once charged it will run for days. There's a switch on the bottom which allows you to toggle easily between your devices. My only issue is the charging port on the underside, where it might have been better on one of the ends. And though it still feels small in my hand while in use, the feel is good. It works quite well, and it's easy to see that over time the T630 will become a favorite when going mobile.11/27/2013

$review_text.: First of all this is a great hard drive, but if you spend just a few $s more you can get twice the capacity, so look for atleast a 250 GB drive.Note: If you want to skip the long review, you can go to the last paragraph of this review where I have some useful tips on how best to use your portable drive and how to keep ideal data backup.It is a given fact that any portable drive you buy in the market today is going to perform good in the short term - maybe 3 months, 6 months or even a year.But when you are buying a portable drive - you have to look beyond 3-5 years because thats how long you are probably going to keep your drive. You have to look at the reliability of the drive - to not lose any data because of hard disk failures.I have used various drives - Seagate, Western Digital, Hitachi, Samsung .., but I can vouch for the fact that Seagate is the numero uno when it comes to drive reliability. I have had many laptop & portable drives give up on me, but Seagate has never let me down.Seagate is usually bit more expensive than others - but very reliable.About this particular drive:+ It is light weight, has a dim light indicator on one of the sides which tells that the drive is plugged in+ Neat sleek casing which makes it look good+ Thick and flexible USB cable which makes it easy to plug the drive without any fear of breaking/twiching the cable+ Very light weight drive+ Comes with the Ceedo software which will make your desktop applications portable (I have never used it myself, but there are good reviews about this software on the internet)What I do not like about the drive:- I wish if it was packed with some better backup software like SecondCopyTip #1: Backup software=======================Ok, now that you have a backup drive, how do you plan to use it to backup your data on your laptop/desktop ? I use a software called SecondCopy - which I found to be very addictive to use:- Once you have this software installed, you can select all the folders on your desktop/laptop that you want to backup and also select the destination where you want to backup- You can configure the backup profile in such a way that either automatically or manually, the software will find the differences between the 2 drives and display the differences to you and let you backup data from your laptop/desktop on to your drive.Tip #2: Secondary Backup=========================+ Now, that you have all your backup setup and you throw in your drive in your laptop bag and unfortunately you leave your laptop bag in your car and your laptop along with your backup drive is stolen, what do you do in this case where you have lost your primary data as well as your backup data - there are 2 options- Do not keep your portable drive in the same bag in which you carry your laptop, which is a bit of an inconvinience- Or, you buy another drive - you can either buy a similar drive or buy a 3.5" big hard drive(which needs external power supply) and keep it at home and keep your backups on both the portable drive as well as the big drive which you have at your home - this way even if you lose your laptop bag or even if you lose your big hard drive at home, there is another backup from which you can retrieve your dear data - your photos, your projects, your movies, music ...Tip #3: Network drive======================This is the ultimate nirvana of any drive. Basically you will have to buy a network drive device and connect this to your hard disk, once you do that and do some additional configuration, you can let your drive be available on your home network - this way, you can listen to your music/watch movies that are there on your hard disk from any computer in your home/from an Apple TV .... Or you can even leave your hard disk at home and access the data from outside of your home(from office/anywhere else there is internet). The network drive comes with its own security settings etc, so you do not have to worry about a hacker accessing your drive.
$review_summary.: The best portable drive out in the market - but try to spend a few $s more and get a bigger drive

$prod_ID.: B00HH0YBJC
$reviewDate.: 12 17, 2013
$REVIEW.: First, let me state that Anker supplied me with a sample of this product free of charge in return for my honest and fair evaluation of it.  What follows is my personal opinion and has in no way been influenced by Anker.I already have a case that I love for my iPad, but wanted a keyboard and a case that would hold both.  First, let me talk about the keyboard.  I love it!  This is the first compact BT keyboard I've owned and I find that I use it surprisingly often, much more than I anticipated.  The keyboard feels solid and well constructed as all Anker products I've owned do.  It charges via a USB cable either through a computer USB port or with a 5V AC charger.  I charged the device fully before using.  It only took about 1 1/2 hours to be fully charged and there is an indicator light that stays on during charging and goes off when charge is complete.  Other reviews state that the same light flashes when battery gets low, but I haven't been able to run it down that far since I've had it.The keyboard pairing process is extremely simple.  You just press the connect button and then the iPad gives you a code to enter on the keyboard and you're done.  The keys are a little firm for my taste but I imagine they'll wear in over time and I'd much prefer them to be a bit firm than a bit sloppy.  Keystrokes have a nice tactility and I haven't had any issues with missed strokes or sticking keys which seem to be common issues with BT and compact keyboards in general.  The keyboard is extremely thin and very light.  It works well for me on my lap or on my desk and the size makes it easy to hold with one hand and type with the other when necessary.  There is an On/Off toggle switch as well that should make the battery last for several months for the casual user.  Even for the constant user, it has a Lion battery which doesn't suffer from memory or charge fatigue issues so you can charge it as often as you like with no fear of degraded life or overcharging.Now the case... When I first unboxed the product, I was immediately pleased with the look and feel of the case.  It has a slightly textured exterior and a very attractive black finish.  The asthetics of the case are nice and the magnetic flap that folds over blends well into the case design.  The inside is a nice gray &#34;sued-type&#34; material that feels good and works well with the rubberized insert that secures the iPad to stand the device up.  The insert secures the iPad well without obscuring any portion of the screen and leaves access to all buttons and ports.  There is a round cutout in the case for the rear camera as well.Unfortunately the case has some drawbacks that, in my opinion, keep it from being a viable option for use.  First, the keyboard is secured to the case magnetically.  The problem is that it's not really secured very well at all.  The keyboard slides all over the place.  If you fold the bottom of the case over to close it, the keyboard slides all the way down and you have to re-position it to close it all the way.  If you pick up the open case, say to move across the room, without holding the keyboard, it'll slide and likely fall off completely if you're going far.  While the magnetic attachment is convenient, the design needs to be re-worked a bit to make it &#34;stick&#34; a little better.Secondly, the case doesn't have magnets to turn the iPad On/Off using the smartlock feature.  It's likely that the keyboard prevents simple implementation of this and I guess I'm spoiled, but I don't think I'll go back to a case that doesn't have that functionality.Finally, the case liner and the rubberized insert work well to hold the iPad at an angle...sorta.  The first issue I have is that when the keyboard is on the case, the iPad stands almost straight upright.  This isn't a good angle for anything.  On my lap I can't see the screen at all.  On my desk, I have to lean over to see it well.  So you have to take the keyboard off the case to use it.  You can move it partially off the case and get a good angle, but then they keyboard rocks on the case edge.  So this isn't a solution for having a good &#34;laptop&#34; type setup where the screen and keyboard are fixed together and can be easily used while sitting in a chair or laying in bed.  Removing the keyboard allows the screen to be positioned better.  But, the angles it can be stood at are severely limited because eventually the friction between the rubber and the &#34;suede&#34; is insufficient and the device slips down.  It would be nice if it had recesses under the keyboard to allow it to be positioned at shallower angles when the keyboard is removed.So, in summary,  I love this keyboard and will be using it for the foreseeable future.  However, I'll be using the case I already had and just keeping the keyboard separate.  The case tries hard, but just doesn't make the cut.  If the keyboard stayed secure and the device stood at a usable angle I'd bump it to 4 stars at this price point.  Smartlock compatibility and more versatility in the device angle when the keyboard is removed would get 5 stars.  But they keyboard alone doesn't justify the price and for me, that's the only usable thing I got.  So the keyboard alone - 5 stars.  The case alone - 2 stars.  And with the price point factored in, I think it comes out to the 3 stars I gave it.

$REVIEW.: The EasyAcc 4 in 1 is a router, a battery charger, a flash drive and SD card reader, that enables wireless sharing and wireless storage.I've tried a few wireless sharing devices like this, and their most important use is to expand the storage capacity of limited storage devices like phones or tablets.Some have built in storage. This one doesn't. You have to connect memory to this, and then connect up with this via its own wifi signal, in order to get the extra storage.What this has, that many others don't, is an SD card slot, which would make it useful for photographers, who can use this on the road to upload what they've shot and share it directly with those who need to see it. It also, in addition to having a battery, has a built in charger with enough juice (8800mAh) to charge a phone a few times and a tablet maybe once.It also has an ethernet input - so that it works as a temporary router, or allows you to get the internet at the same time as you are upload your files. Of course, I'm only likely to use this much when I am on the road, and can't just plug devices into my laptop, and certainly won't have access to an ethernet cable, so I don't find that to be very useful but imagine it might be for some.The app they offer is not very intuitive, and the instructions aren't very clear. Only tech-savvy folks should bother with this. I was given this product by the manufacturer to test and try out for the purpose of a review. I was at first excited by the various possibilities - and I think that this could be just the thing for some folks, but I have to admit that this is likely to end up in my drawer of rarely-used gadgets. I've got chargers, and I've got external hard drives, including some that transmit their own wireless signal and are self-powered and that I find to be more intuitive and convenient than this one. The SD card slot could come in handy but it would be nice to have a micro SD and Compact Flash port there as well - if you really just need wireless transmission from an SD card, I'd suggestthis Wifi Sd Cardthat will transmit files without even removing it from your camera.

$REVIEW.: After purchasing my iPad 3 six months ago, I decided to also purchase the Smart Cover in blue leather to go with it. A short time later,  I purchased a thin back case made by Belkin to protect the case from from scratches..  This combination looked and felt great. The dark blue top cover with the transluscent shell on the backside.What made me change my iPad case the first time, is when I dropped the iPad about 3 feet.  I was fortunate that the fall was onto soft carpet, and the iPad survived just fine, but the Belkin case snapped off and was loose after this.  If the fall had been onto concrete, I doubt the thin Belkin shell would have protected the iPad from damage.  It!s designed for scratch protection, but not falls.I next purchased the Griffin Survivor which gave the iPad great protection.  The biggest problem with the Survivor is that it was bulky, heavy, and access to iPad features like the camera are covered with a rubber flap.  Every time I took a photo, I needed to lift the flap and hold it in position with my finger.  The rubber stays to hold the flaps open, did not work well at all.  Since I don't use my iPad in severe conditions like hurricanes and dust storms, I retired the Survivor and returned to my original set up.  The blue leather Smart Cover and the thin Belkin back shield.I began reading other people's reviews on cases and watching reviews on You Tube.  I was looking for a case that had the following features:  well made, a professional look, a stable stand, easy to use, light weight, unobstructed openings, and capable of taking a moderate fall onto concrete without damage to the iPad.Eureka. I finally found what I was looking for. The Ridge by Devicewear.  The Vegan leather feels similar to my iPad leather Smart Cover and is even the same dark blue color that I like.  The fit of the case is perfect and the thickness of the shell is at least double that of the Belkin.  It looks like it would protect the iPad from a moderate fall onto a hard surface.  The overall look of the case is professional.  Slim, lightweight, and appearing much more expensive than it actually was.  The openings are unobstructed so taking a photo is easy.  Also the Ridge system works great.  All the viewing angles are very stable, in sharp contrast to what I was accustomed to with the unstability of Apple Smart Cover set-upAlso the touch of the inner portion of the Devicewear cover feels like rich velvet and I actually prefer the feel of this cover to the inner portion of the Apple Smart Cover.  When you close both covers, a magnet turns off the iPad.  Both the Devicewear and Apple cover work the same in this regard.  They both work very well.Since nothing is perfect, I worked diligently to find fault with this product.  The only two things I could come up with were minor.  My dock speaker can't be used with the Ridge cover on and I wish the opening for the on/off button were a bit larger.  Maybe a holder for a stylus would be nice, but since I infrequently use a stylus, I didn't find this to be a drawback. Also, I only stand my iPad in landscape mode and have no use for it to stand in vertical mode.  I also don't like the style of the multiple viewing cases.All in all, this is a great iPad case at a very reasonable price.  The first day I brought my Ridge iPad case to work, a colleague liked mine so much, that he ordered one in black for his iPad.  Hats off to Devicewear for developing an excellent product at a very reasonable price.  This case is worth every cent, and then some.

There are also leather segments over the centers of the straps that act as spacers when the cover is closed, keeping the cover off the face of the Kindle

As others have mentioned, if you fold the magnetic closure strap back, then the front cover, the magnet will hold the cover back very securely
I've been using this cover for just a couple of weeks now, and am completely satisfied with it's quaility and convenience

It is attractive, well made, and well designed protection for the Kindle 4.

$reviewerName.: Donald E. Fulton
$Helpful?.: [2, 3] $reviewDate.: 07 26, 2013
$REVIEW.: (update) I find my review written about Nook HD included here for an entirely different model tablet. Amazon or B*N this is unethical!D.F.---------------Nook HD overviewGreat screen, no cameras, weak speakers, crappy battery life, compromised android OS, but an inexpensive way to browse web and run the world of android apps on a fast, beautiful display. Plus it has a microSD slot to hold lots of videos for offline viewing. And of course, its original purpose, to provide a slick interface for purchase and reading of magazines and books.PlusesWide range of browers available. I have 9 on my machine. All browsers for tablets have reduced functionality so some browsers are better than others for specific tasks. For example, Firefox will play video in HD and does not redirect to mobile sites. Tint and Zirco have a homepage that will access a local html file. With several browsers installed it's easier to get around site restrictions. Firefox has an addon that auto-deletes cookies. Chrome allows spoken search inputs.The world of 700,000 android apps can now be accessed on Nook HD including big and nice apps: Google earth, Skype, YouTube in HD, Adobe Reader, WiFi Analyzer, WiFi Fixer (essential Wifi tool), Google maps, best solitaire ever (by MobilityWare), and free 'run' games. Custom moving backgrounds on Nook HD home screens are fun.AnnoyancesIn two months I have not figured out how to add a browser link to Nook HD home page. Some browsers have the option to add a link to the homepage, but it never works! (It must be that the Nook HD OS does not allow this)Poor battery life, by test I get only 4 hours.Adroid apps normally just suspend, so it tends to take too many presses and taps to cleanly start an application.Audio does not shut off when you exit most radio and music apps. With no OS support for shutting apps down I often have to resort to a reset to silence them.Built-in email has a short time window so you only see few or no messages. Apps like FastHotMail can provide workaround.Screen capture is clumsy (pushing Home and Vol- requires a lot of force and nearly simultaneous pushes).Nook HD not really useful for music, sans headphones, because sound volume on speakers is relatively low.Setting up icons on home screens is kind of a pain. Half of the main screen is taken up by a carousel that cannot be removed. The Nook recommended way of moving an icon to an adjacent screen is to hold icon overlapping the edge, but I find this hit or miss, it only seems reliable after a reset.File directories can be accessed via USB, but have some annoyances: Many file managers have a hard time finding personal files lost in a maze of OS directories. Nook HD allows deletion of its standard user directories (like 'kids B&N; files') only to later write them back again.Tablet does not reliably remember some settings. Occasionally I find the screen will be dim or the notification is too loud and when I look the setting has changed.No way (that I have found) to add personal data for quick entry.(update)Bluetooth keyboard problem solvedI have an inexpensive bluetooth keyboard that works fine with another tablet (Blackberry Playbook), but I could not get it to work with Nook HD. It would pair fine, but nothing happened when keys are hit. I see others complaining of this too. Finally I solved the problem with an app called BlueInput (available on Play Store). It now does the pairing, not Nook OS, and you select the bluetooth keyboard using 'Switch Keyboard' icon.(update)Fix for adding web link icons to the home page. Some browsers have the option to add a bookmark to Home, but this never seemed to work in Nook HD. I think I now understand the source of the problem. The default Nook HD launcher (with carousel) ignores them. The work around is to install the Nova launcher, and it will show them on the home screens.

" devices perform the same--I have one of these in a another room that works better, with more positive "clicks" as you set each source, and which rarely fails to pass through the program signal.So I'd guess that these are just inexpensively built and are consequently imprecise due to the materials used in their construction.Overall I like the product--they are inexpensive, and that's usually good--yet they perform inconsistently from one unit to the next
Nevertheless they get the job done at a far better price than many competing items.If your application is "mission-critical" skip these

$reviewer.ID.: A23NSKTMSPPBTR
$prod_ID.: B0042SGDVG
$reviewDate.: 03 8, 2011
$review_text.: Based on reviews, I thought these would be good drives to use to upgrade my RAID based system.  In all fairness, these are not RE drives, but 2TB RE drives cost more than I wanted to spend. My older drives were Samsung RE drives, but only 1TB each.RAID edition drives are nice to have. They coordinate with each other. They are fault tolerant in ways that individual drives are not. They power up and down in sequence, so when I turn my computer off or put it to sleep, I hear the drives turn off at one second intervals with the computer powering down one second after the final drive. They survived catastrophic "blue screen" Windows failures without ever having to rebuild. And nicest of all, their performance blew these 2TB drives away.With these 2TB drives in non-RAID mode, I was able to get speeds that were in the neighborhood of what other reviewers were getting. In RAID0 mode, I was shockingly disappointed. I'm using an Intel controller that uses their matrix RAID technology. With the older RE drives, I was able to have a lightning fast RAID0 array for the OS, a very fast RAID0 volume (in the Windows sense of volume) for ephemeral media, or anything I could afford to lose in a catastrophe, although I never once lost anything due to hardware or controller problems. I also had a RAID5 backup partition for my OS, and a large RAID5 partition that offered reasonable protection for my other data. (I still backed things up regularly of course.) In my configuration, all media libraries were kept off the OS disk, so I could restore the OS quickly if needed without needing to worry about data files, and vice versa.I tried replicating the environment with these drives. I was able to get usable performance out of them, but if I tried copying huge files across the network, the performance of the OS became degraded significantly. I never got throughput on the RAID0 volume that came close to the RAID5 volume, although it should have been much faster. Ultimately, I ended up using one drive stand-alone, and putting two of them in a RAID1 array. The performance is more than adequate for my purposes, but it's still possible to run things that cause momentary pauses in other tasks.Some people are concerned with the 5400 RPM speed. In reality, the platters are the same size as they were for my 1TB drives, so the heads need to move about half the distance to read the same amount of contiguous data. Rotations take longer, but the net effect of 5400RPM is not what users might expect.I use the computer primarily as a media center. Assuming the average one hour HD TV program is 7GB, and I want to record four shows at once, watch another, and stream another to another part of the house, I don't want to lose speed. But considering that all this happens in real time, it's only 1/3600 of the file that is read or written per second on average, so the throughput will still far exceed my needs. But if I want to copy one of those recordings across my network, I can no longer do it in 2.5 minutes, let alone without affecting performance. The saving grace is that my OS is on a disk that's separate from much of my data.Overall, the performance is not stellar, and you can't expect to get RE performance out of these. But you can expect to get performance that is very good for the price, and my history with Samsung drives has made me feel comfortable with their reliability. These drives are certainly quiet enough for my media center, so overall they may be the best (but not ideal) solution to my current need. Windows 7 gives them a WEI score of 5.9 on my system, which doesn't seem much worse than the 6.3 that my old drives got.  But I would not recommend copying several files of a few hundred GB concurrently while expecting the computer to maintain full performance on everything else.

$review_text.: An SSD was the most logical upgrade for my otherwise well-spec'd Lenovo T530 laptop. I was already familiar with, and confident in the Samsung 8xx Pro series from several desktop PCs I've worked with.Good preparation was the key to an accurate and speedy installation. Even before I ordered the SSD, I reorganized the HDD free space so that my C: drive partition could be reduced to fit onto Samsung's 256 GB product. With this laptop I had already used the &#34;bare metal recovery&#34; procedure available with my Windows Home Server 2011 system, so that was the migration method of choice. I ensured a timely backup of the original HDD on the server, performed the actual component switch-over in a few minutes (having already consulted the Lenovo T530 owner's manual), then booted from the WHS 2011 client recovery CD. About 25 minutes later I rebooted my recovered Windows 7 system from the new SSD.The only trace of an anomaly was the next day while syncing my iPhone, when iTunes complained it wasn't authorized for the apps on the phone. When I authorized the computer, it complained the computer was already authorized. I can only guess that iTunes does some additional hardware signature matching to check authorization validity and that the HDD to SDD transition confused it.Following the upgrade, I downloaded and installed Samsung's Magician application (though I removed it's shortcut from the Startup folder to avoid an annoying dialog box when rebooting). I followed most of Magician's suggestions for optimizing the system for SDD based on the reliability objective.The T530 is now very quick on its toes. Even large applications like Photoshop now seem to snap open. If you've already got 8 GB RAM or greater, this is definitely an upgrade worth going for.When planning your new partition layout for an SSD upgrade, be sure to note when &#34;1 GB&#34; means &#34;1x10^9 bytes&#34; (the traditional interpretation) vs. contexts where it means &#34;2^30 bytes&#34; (computer geek interpretation, as displayed in many places in Microsoft products). The usable capacity of the Samsung 256GB model is 256 GB (traditional interpretation), equivalent to 238.47 GB (computer geek). The figures shown in Microsoft's Disk Management partition layout display are based on 2^30. Right-click and open Properties of your C: drive to see both styles of figures side-by-side.

Even then though, it's clearly not going to provide the kind of coverage a full security system would, even using some external cameras, simple entry through a window or other location around the house to avoid detection would always be an issue, as well as false alerts from other people approaching the house. While away from home I tried the online viewing and wasn't particularly impressed with it. I also had a lot of problems with it constantly dropping the video feed, and having to wait for it to re-acquire. This happened constantly and with a good strong internet connection so did not make me feel particularly inclined to upgrade the service.Overall, I had mixed feelings. If you don't mind paying the $80/year for the Premium service, this might be a worthwhile product, particularly to monitor activities at your home and/or business while you are not there. I'm not sure it is quite sufficient to provide true home security, but it might be an option to consider if you just want some basic security.

I was thinking that I might have to go to an normal Backpack and forget about finding a bag with a deicated slot for this massive computer, when I read about this bag and decided that I would give it a shot.With the computer in its dedicated slot in the Titan, I have room for the cooling table, LG power brick, gaming mouse, Zalman clipon speakers, 3g/4g router with mobile modem(in its original box), the 3d glasses (again in the original box), an external 2gig hard drive and my Ipad 2(with stand). There is still room for more things with all the pockets and the way it can be organized.It rained/snowed all day the other day and the backpack repelled it, I put on the rain bag just to see how it fit and was very happy to see it shed all the rain.The price is a bit more for the Titan than I could have bought a regular backpack or even the largest Laptop backpack but is well worth it when you think of all the stuff you can carry around in the same bag. The price is offset by conviance of such a large bag and the fact you now have a bag that definately protects your equipment. The 180 degree swiveling Laptop section is definately a boon.

$REVIEW.: For me, this camera was an upgrade.  I am a purse-sized point and shoot user (e.g., Canon Elph, Kodak EasyShare).  However, i'm finding that (1) I don't carry a camera around much anymore due to the improvements in cell phone cameras and (2) the shutter speed of point and shoots is frustrating such that I constantly miss shots waiting for the darn camera to focus and take the picture.  I got the opportunity to try this camera out and I was very impressed with the lightening fast speed and picture quality.  I can't compare with a DSLR because I've never used one, but compared to the relatively cheap cameras I typically use, it is impressively fast.  I think it does really well in low light.  I took some pictures on Halloween night, for example, and they came out really good.  I was surprised/impressed.  I didn't even think my flash went off!  So this does way better tha the cameras I have used in the past in low light settings.  It is also really easy to take video (caution, the video button is easy to hit by mistake) and there are tons of different settings that you can experiment with.  The zoom is really nice and adjusts very easily.  Unlike a poket sized point and shoot, I had to actually read the manual pretty carefully - several times.  This camera isn't as user friendly to a novice, although it's far easier to use than a DSLR (as far as I can tell).  There has been a learning curve though.  I found this camera to be intimidating at first, but after I took a few hours and mixed manual reading with some online videos (all with the camera in hand) I began to feel more confident when using it.I am not a camera guru, so I can't really speak to the special features etc. compared to a truly high end camera.  My understanding is that this is an entry level "nicer" camera.  I've honestly never used a DSLR - they scare this novice - and I am not completely clear on the tradeoffs.  What I can speak to is this - if you are a true amateur photographer, like many of us are, but crave better pictures, this is a good pick. I think this camera is a great choice for people who want more than a point and shoot or cellphone camera but who are not really avid photographers such that a DSLR is a wise purchase choice.  This isn't a camera to carry around every day - it's bigger than whet I am used to.  But you can take nice pictures and the shutter speed is great for parents who know that you have precious few seconds to snap a picture where your baby or toddler is cooperating or looking at you.  Also, you can change around lenses.  I don't have other lenses (and I'm not sure why I'd need any) but my understanding is that this camera works with other lenses in the Fujifim X series.  It's also small enough/light enough to take with you on vacation.  I haven't done this yet, but I will be taking it to Disney World.

$REVIEW.: As a first time PDA buyer, the TJ27 is exactly what I was looking for.  Essentially, I wanted a handheld device that would let me store, edit, create, and synchronize MS Word documents, keep an address book, memopad and scheduler, plus take a few snapshots without having to lug a full size camera around.  Of course, these days, most PDAs will do all of the above, but I wanted something with an attractive design, plus good color resolution, a minimum of 32 megs internal memory, plus Memory Stick option, and at a resonable price.  This particular model satisfied all of those needs.Upon registering with Sony you're issued a code that allows you to download a free copy of Documents-To-Go Professional, the software that enables you to use MS Word and Excel documents on the PDA.  The Clie installation disk comes with Data Export (lets you use the Memory Stick as a removable drive on your PC), Palm Desktop for Clie, HotSynch and much more.  Unfortuntely, most of the additional software included is of the time limited or stripped down variety, most of which I decided not to load.  So far, the unit has held up well, producing pictures that are adequate for emailing or viewing on the PC desktop, and documents that synch flawlessly with the originals on my hard drive.  Both keypad and Grafitti Pad are functional and comfortable in relation to the overall size of the device, although using the Grafitti Pad takes some practice.The only real drawback I see is that the battery can't be easily replaced by the user, however, it does fill up pretty quick after the initial charge.  And I would have gladly paid an additional $20-$30 bucks to have a cradle (very difficult to find in the stores) included in the package rather than wires, but that's just a personal preference.  Overall, I'm quite happy with this device.

Neither of these things are show stoppers, so I think the lens rates 4 stars.

$review_text.: I got three Dell D610 laptops from a client after they were being decommissioned. The laptops needed RAM, a bigger HDD, wireless, and Bluetooth. Everything was installed into the laptop, XP Pro 32bit was installed, and I installed the TP-Link driver for this card. It seems to work fine, until your laptop goes to sleep. Once you wake it up, you will find that the CPU is being used at 50% constantly until you reboot. I tracked the problem to this card and contacted TP-Link. They had me try an alternate driver with the same issue. I then went to the chipset manufacturer (Atheros) and downloaded the driver directly from them, for their chipset. Have not had a problem since.In other words, if you purchase this card do NOT use the TP-Link drivers, even the latest ones from their site. You WILL have problems if your laptop goes to sleep or hibernates. Just download the Atheros 9220X driver from Atheros and you will be very happy with the product.

The sound quality was great, but the amp wasn't pushing much power at all. The sound quality of this amp is very close to amps that cost more than 2x its price.I really recommend this amp, but take into consideration that I could not get it to work well in bridged mode.

$reviewer.ID.: A2W9GX82SLKROQ
$productID.: B00A659HXK
$rev_NAME.: Lenny
$Helpful?.: [3, 3] $review_date.: 05 19, 2013
$review_text.: First, this is an analog camera. It is meant to be used with an analog video recorder that can control the pan tilt through its RS485 port using either Pelco-D or Pelco-P protocol.A few other reviews mentioned the lack of a remote control. I'm not sure if things have changed, but the checklist on my box did not mention a remote control, and indeed none is included. The length of the all-in-one cable is also 60 ft, not 100 ft. If you're expecting the remote and 100 ft of cable, you might be disappointed. Q-See's website also mentioned the remote and 100 ft of cable, so perhaps we were all sent the wrong unit.It does come with two mounting options (ceiling and wall mount), 60 feet of cable (not 100ft as Amazon's description indicated), and a 110-240V power adapter. The output of the adapter is 12V 1.2A. There's even a small flat head screwdriver included. Too bad there's no Philips head screwdriver for opening up the unit if you need to adjust the serial settings (more on this later). The mounts allow you to run cables internally, or alternatively there's a notch to run your cables along the wall or ceiling.When panning, the entire plastic dome will rotate, not just the image sensor and IR LEDs inside. This is probably because the partition between the IR LEDs and the image sensor protrudes out from the plastic dome slightly, to prevent the IR light from being reflected by the dome back to the camera and light sensor. I think that's a well thought out design. I have seen outdoor IR cameras where there's no separation between the IR and the image sensor, causing nighttime image to be pretty washed out. There is a light sensor located below the image sensor. When tilting, only the interior parts move.The camera has DIP switches that allows you to change its address (1 - 16), baud rate (1200, 2400, 4800 or 9600 bps) and protocol (Pelco-D or Pelco-P). You will need different addresses if you have more than one camera with a RS485 control connected to your video recorder.Q-See or Amazon needs to clarify what comes with the package, but assuming what I received is accurate, this is a solidly constructed and well designed camera for outdoor use. It is fairly expensive, however, and I would seriously consider spending an extra $80 (current pricing) for the version with 3x optical zoom.
$review_summary.: Solid construction, pan / tilt feature might be usable with other systems

$reviewer.NAME.: Desired FX "Call me Don. It's shorter than Is...
$No. helps.: [0, 3] $reviewDate.: 11 4, 2011
$REVIEW.: There's really no point to buying theLinksys RE1000unless you've got a portion of your property where you really can't get a wifi signal. Using it to strengthen an existing, usable signal in a remote part of the house is a spotty proposition, at best: for every extra bar of signal you get, you get a commensurate amount of signal drops.In my instance, I have my wifi set up on the first floor and use my PS3 and iPad primarily on the third floor. There's a very low level signal up there, but not so low that it can't connect, and I've never had it outright drop. I set the RE1000 up in an outlet on the third floor and it bumped me up a notch or two in signal strength, but then it dropped signal at least once an hour. Whatever I gained in signal strength, I lost in reliability.On the plus side, it's very, very easy to set-up: plug it into an outlet near your wifi transmitter and run the software on your computer. The software on the included disc said it was incompatible with OS X Lion, so I went to the Web site and downloaded the newest version, which worked immediately.You start the install software and it searches for the RE1000. When your computer finds the extender, it displays all the wifi signals the extender detects and asks which network you'd like to join. Select (and provide your password) and the extender will pair itself to the network in much the same way that Bluetooth devices do. Once the extender is paired, move it to an outlet toward the limits of your wifi range, near the area where you would like to use your devices, then try to connect with your notebook machine, or your tablet, or your game console. If all goes well, you'll see your wifi network just as if you were set up in the same room.I'm in the process of moving, and while my new place has a strong wifi signal, there are places in the house where it's very weak or completely unreliable. I'll try setting up the RE1000 there and then report if it performs better when I'm using it in a manner more appropriate to its design.UPDATE 11/25/11: I've set it up in the new venue and it's performing well. I did discover that I had to restart some devices after setting it up; otherwise, they seemed confused by the choice between the native signal and the extender's wifi.In addition, I had to take my work computer home recently. The wifi hardware switch on it doesn't work, so I had to hook it up with an RJ45 cable run from the computer to the extender. It worked seamlessly, and turned out to be a great feature for me that I never expected I would need.
$review_summary.: Very easy to set up...just remember, it's an extender, not a booster.

$productID.: B00CXAKQEU
$reviewDate.: 04 22, 2014
$review_text.: There was a strong static field created when I removed the protective cover.  This static electricity attracted lint and tiny bits of dirt that ended up becoming tiny unremovable bubbles.  This happened with both of the original two skins I purchased.  Assuming that I had been careless, I ordered another package of two.  Even though I was very, very careful, my results with the second pair of skins was no better than the first.  I will freely admit that I am very picky but these results were unacceptable to me.  I am going to try another brand.MAJOR UPDATEAfter reading the website of a competing product, I learned the method to eliminate lint from the installation.  I have found that this is a problem that is commonplace in all of these products.  The solution is to install the product and then place a small bit of tape on the outside edge near any lint that needs to be removed.  This piece of tape becomes the "handle" to lift the edge in order to remove lint as follows.  Use the tape "handle" to peel back the skin to expose the lint.  Use another piece of tape curved backwards into a loop exposing the sticky side to touch and remove each piece of lint.  I find that wide packaging clear tape seems to work best for me.  I have been able to successfully remove all pieces of lint and so I am upgrading this review to five stars.
$Helpful?.: [0, 1] $SUMMARY.: Attracts lint and dirt during installation

$review_text.: I really like this little device.  Build is first rate with redundant LAN and power connections as well as the best drive mechanism in the class which forgoes caddies while securely locking the drives in place.  You also get a LCD display up front, though honestly I've never used it.  It's all rather quiet, and thus far has offered bullet proof reliability.  My needs have me using this as a storage server, not for real time use.  I've found that I can get 40MB/S writes consistently, which is well below my Synology (8 drive array, so not a fair comparison).  That being said, it's still rather fast, but I wouldn't want to run a database off of it or edit media files stored on it.  Neither really seems to be the intended use.Compared to Synology (I have an 1812+, but others work similarly):Pros* Available with WD Red drives (great drives) or bring your own* Easy drive installation without caddies (best I've seen)* Much faster initial setup* Simpler interface* Redundant power & lan (vs redundant lan only)* Significantly less expensiveCons* Limited extended functionality & apps* Not expandable to additional enclosures* Traditional RAID (0, 1, 10, 5) as opposed to more scalable solutions* No file manager* Much slower (I can use the Synology for my Lightroom files, which I cannot with the WD)note some of these cons can be quite significant for some users and not at all an issue for othersCompared to Seagate Business Storage Windows Server 4-Bay NAS (more of an apples to apples comparison)Pros* Easy drive installation without caddies (best I've seen)* Much faster (and easier) initial setup (Seagate requires a keyboard and monitor)* Simpler interface (Seagate's Windows Storage Server 8 can become quite overwhelming)* Redundant power & lan (vs redundant lan only)* Significantly less expensiveCons* Limited extended functionality & apps* Traditional RAID (0, 1, 10, 5) as opposed to more scalable solutions* No file managerCompared to a two drive array (like the WD My Cloud EX2)Pros* More efficient redundancy of raid 5 (lose 25% of capacity vs 50%)* Faster reads and writes (no scientific testing, but I own and use both)* Redundancy of LAN and power connections* Greater capacityCons* Higher priceI highly recommend that people back up their data and they do so with redundancy (using RAID isn't a backup in itself, but your backup should have redundancy).

$reviewer.ID.: ANIIUK21KSTIW
$prod_ID.: B002GHBW52
$reviewDate.: 10 17, 2009
$review_text.: Great Performance...This card has breathed new life into my aging PC.  I installed this in a PC with a Socket 754 Sempron64 3100+ CPU.  Running Win XP Pro with 1.5GB RAM.  Replaced an NVidia 6200.  This PC is used as an HTPC and is connected to a projection TV via Component Video.  I do not play any games on it, just run SageTV software with multiple TV capture devices.  My old video card was unable to playback 1080i MPEG-2 or any HD-h.264 videos.  This Diamond ATI Radeon HD4650 AGP card plays everything flawlessly (provided I am using codecs that are able to use hardware acceleration) with either Overlay mode or VMR-9 Renderless (Full Screen Exclusive).  Regular VMR-9 works when playing back in windowed mode, but there is some stuttering during full-screen playback of HD MPEG-2 content with plain VMR-9.Using the ATI MPEG codec with DXVA hardware acceleration to play back MPEG-2 content full-screen on a 1080i TV, CPU usage maxes out at about 45% for 1080i content, 40% for 720p, and 20% for 480i.  Using the MPC-HC h.264 codec to play a 720p file required only about 15% CPU.  I am still unable to watch Hulu content at full screen, but this is because there are currently no hardware accelerated codecs for playing back FLASH content, and my Sempron 3100 just doesn't have enough power to handle it.Questionable Specs...The picture shown on the Amazon page is still incorrect.  The installation guide has a diagram that looks like the picture on Amazon's website, but it's wrong too.  The card has 2 DVI connectors and one round S-Video connector.  The package includes 1 DVI to VGA adapter, 1 DVI to HDMI adapter, 1, S-Video to Composite adapter, and 1 S-Video to Component (HDTV) adapter.  The heat-sink and fan look different too.  Oh, and the PCB is green, not red.The Box says 512MB DDR2 on the front, but the side of the box says 512MB DDR3.  Inside the Catalyst Control Panel, it reports the card as having DDR2 memory.  The Diamond website lists it as DDR3.  There are several other manufactures building HD4650 cards, but from what I can tell all the others used DDR2 (though some had 1024MB).The Diamond Website says a 300W power supply is required, but the box says 400W.  All the other manufacturers that make HD4650 cards seem to recommend 400W.  My computer has a 300W supply, and it seems to be OK.Poor Power Connector Design...The card requires more power than the AGP bus can provide, so it has an auxiliary power connector (6-pin, 12V).  It also includes a 6-pin to 4-pin molex adaptor, in case you have an older power supply that doesn't have one of the 6-pin connectors.  The problem is that this connector is on the front of the card (top-left) and sticks straight out.  There is no way to plug power into this card without interfering with the first PCI slot on most ATX or mini-ATX motherboards.  I was fortunate that I could put a half-height card in that first slot, because a full height card not fit next to this video card.  It's a shame they did this, because it is otherwise a nice single-slot card.  There are a couple of other manufactures building these HD4650 cards, but they all appear to have the power connector in the same place.  It would be much better if they rotated the connector 90 degrees or mounted it on the back of the board.This is a medium-sized video card.  Length-wise, this card just barely fits in my Silverstone LC-17 case.  It is a little longer than the old 6200 video card it is replacing.  Even with the fan it does fit in a single slot, but as mentioned above, the power connector is likely to interfere with one of your PCI slots.The fan is super quiet (even with the case open and my head a few inches away, I can't hear it over the LC-17 case fans.One other note, when you first set the card up, you must connect a monitor to one of the DVI connectors (you can use the VGA adaptor).  You cannot get the HDTV output setup correctly the first time if you just connect it straight to the Component HDTV connector.  Once you get it setup, you can disconnect the monitor and everything works great.Bottom line...Although there are some discrepancies between the data published at Amazon's website, Diamond's website, and the product packaging, and the power connector is layed out poorly, I am happy with the performance I am getting with the card.

$reviewer.ID.: A27SEH7FJJIKIC
$productID.: B004HJ545G
$reviewerName.: BF
$Helpful?.: [12, 12] $review_date.: 10 15, 2012
$review_text.: There's a lot of good functionality built into this unit.  It has pretty much the widest variety of connectors that I've seen on any cable tester.  There are two of each connector:  for each pair one is an "output" and one is an "input" connector.  Output connectors transmit a funny digital test signal, and the input connectors detect this signal and display the results (of which pins on one end of the cable are attached to which pins on the other) on the LED matrix.  You attach one end of a cable to any output connector and the other end to any input connector -- so you can have different connectors on each end of the cord.o You can test a cable with different connectors on the ends.o There is a row of "intermittent" LEDs next to the matrix.  You connect a cable, press the reset button, the wiggle the cable.  If any of the wires are intermittent the corresponding LED will light.  You can repeat this at will to track down a problem spot.o There is a built-in tone generator.  It generates a reasonably clean squarewave at either 440 or 1,000 Hz.  There's a slide switch that selects one of three volume levels, but the output levels are not quite correct:  The peak-to-peak output levels are: "-50MIC"=> 280mV (I think about 28mV would be more realistic),  "-10dBV => 3.0V (should be 0.9V), +4dBu => 3.2V (this is about right).o There is a way to test for shorts in a cable.o There is a way to test cables where the far end can't be plugged into the tester:  you short pins on the other end then test for shorts.o The two pins on the side labeled "SPEAKON" are banana jacks, but are not the standard 3/4" apart so can't be used for testing dual banana plugs.o The LED matrix can only test three pins at a time.  So if you are testing a cable with a plug that has more than three pins (e.g a MIDI or an ethernet plug) then there's a workaround:  The mysterious slide switch that is not described in the manual and whose positions are labeled "SW1", "SW2" and "SW3" is used for this.  The first position lets you test the first three pins of a connector, the second position lets you test the second three pins, and the third position lets you test the third set of three pins.o The LED matrix looks identical to the one on the Behringer CT100 cable tester.  The two units look identical except this one has way more connectors.  I can't believe but that they're the same design and made in the same factory, so I'd buy this one because it tests more connector types.o The instructions (which are printed on the box) don't mention that you need to install two AA batteries.o The box is painted steel, made with reasonable precision, with some scuff marks.  The PC boards inside are clean and well-soldered.  There are some mechanical hacks in the construction:  for example some of the connectors have plastic parts crudely trimmed off to fit, and the sliders of the slide switches have been partly clipped off to make them fit through the narrow, short slots through which they protrude.  I get the impression of these being built by a garage-type operation, but none of these things looks like they would affect reliability or longevity.  I'm confident this will be a rugged and long-lasting tool.
$review_summary.: A good, capable, inexpensive cable tester
