$review_text.: Having checked out several TV's before Christmas, I only found two really good ones that all the critics were raving about. One was a Sony and the other a Samsung. All the techs I spoke with gave these TV's excellent grades. Simply put, you could get the same excellent picture with this Samnsung model A650 as you would with a high end Sony .... but at a cheaper price. Although the picture quality is excellent, you first have to make some adjustments to see that. Pre set factory default settings can be made better by your own adjustments. This set also has the ability to control sound so it keeps the volume constant when those sometimes annoying commercials come on that raise you out of your seat. There are many great features with this TV that work even better when you compliment it with a matching DVD ( also bought a new Samsung VCR/DVD recorder combo). When the telenet option kicks in, you can use one remote (either TV or dvd) to control both sets. The remote that came with the TV is excellent with larger numbers to see. It also has a button that will light up the remote for use at night ... nice feature!I would have given this set 5 stars but I found some minor problems (this set might still deserve 5 stars and maybe I'm too critical). For one thing, picture quality is the sharpest as long as you do not sit any closer than 6 feet. Any closer and there seems to be some distortion. Farther away than 6 feet (up to 18 feet), the picture quality is outstanding. If you're use to watching your set real close than simply buy a 32inch instead. I also noticed that not all channels come in sharp, however I've found out this is not the fault of the set but of the broadcasting channel. The tv sound system is very good but they could have made the bass sound a little deeper and more powerful. You can make this even better by hooking up a theater sound system which results the viewing in a movie theater atmosphere. This set also has the 120mhgz picture speed (others only 60mghz) which catches any blur and smooths them out. I really didn't notice this much as a problem but those who watch a lot of sports (and watch the baseball fly through the air) might appreciate this TV option to stop any blur in movement. Side angle viewing is also excellent allowing up to 180 degree.One last thing ... don't confuse this model with all models of Samsung. Walmart and many other stores were pushing the model 500 or 550T over the Christmas holiday for about a $1000. Those sets do not have all the options, and plugs jacks that the model 650 has. Further, the picture quality and pixel speed are not as good or as fast as with the 650. Don't simply buy a brand and assume they all look and behave alike. Check them out by model numbers and read reviews and product options before making any choice. Sometimes by just spending a couple hundred dollars more will make a tremendous difference and make your viewing more enjoyable. I was also surprised to find a small note in the shipping box that alerted me to the fact my TV might have screen burn in problems if the same picture doesn't move for two hours. I had thought that LCD's didn't have this problem but apparently they do as the old tube sets. Not really a problem unless you use the set for video games and walk a away for a few hours without turning the set off.All in all, I found this set to be really remarkable. It is worth the price and even more if you can get it at a sale price.(As a side note ... my best price was found at Amazon.com)

$review_text.: Not sure I can say enough good things about this router. I'm getting a strong signal, and using the 5Ghz band I'm getting far faster speeds than I did with either my previous router (a 2.4GHz wireless-N) or the 2.4Ghz band on this router. I'm guessing that's not typical I'm using it in a university setting, and am now getting well over 100Mbps).Didn't need the configuraton CD. It did take me a few minutes to figure out how to set it up, as I didn't have a laptop to hook up to it and wanted to place it away from my desktop computer. The quick setup directions only tell you how to configure it by plugging in your computer via an ethernet port, but here's how to do it remotely: Plug in and turn on the router, including the wifi (there's a button on the back). Log onto one of the wifi networks it creates, and use the passwork located on the bottom of the router. Then, type the router's default IP address (which is stated in the user manual available either online or in the provided CD) and you're in. The config menu is straightforward, well designed, and easy to use. Change the name of the networks, update the password to something even more secure, change whether you're broadcasting the SSID, etc... all quite convenient. Tons of advanced features as well, in both the menu settings and the hardware itself. I'll report back once I've had a chance to add a printer to the network, which you can do either via ethernet (if your printer includes networking capabiliy) or USB (if it doesn't). Nice to be able to network a non-network printer. You can also use the USB port to add an external hard drive. I've gotta try that too.Anyway, blazing fast, easy to use, and cheaper than brands that just suck more (I've had trouble with Belkin and D-Link products, for instance). If you're thinking about a new router, this would be a good choice.
$review_summary.: 5Ghz *tripled* my connection speed. Awesome router.

$reviewerName.: Heath Buckmaster "_heath_"
$No. helps.: [0, 0] $review_date.: 11 13, 2009
$review_text.: Air Mouse Elite (with MotionSense), by GyrationLet's jump right in with an assessment of this gadget, which offers a lot of great features, and only one drawback that I've found so far.What do I like?- It's rechargeable, using an included charging station. I _love_ this feature. No batteries to replace, and I have complete freedom of movement (which is a requirement for the "air" aspect of this mouse).- It has the basic mouse functions I expect. Three primary buttons, including a very smooth and consistent trackwheel.- It fits nicely in my hand, and is designed for either left or right handed people.- It's light, even with integrated rechargeable batteries.- Visual cues. When the mouse is being moved there is a blue LED that lights up to let you know there's activity, and a three tier yellow LED that indicates charging status (when attached to the included charging stand).- Highly customizeable buttons. There are three programmable buttons on the top of the mouse. You can REALLY customize these things, and in fact, they can do different things based on the type of program you're in at the time. Let me spend a bit more on this one because this is a major "extra" in this mouse.There are four levels of customization for the top buttons.General: Buttons are defaulted to "Media". This means opening your primary web browser, your email client, and closing the current window.Internet: Buttons are defaulted to: Open home page, Open favourites, Refresh page.Media Player: Buttons are defaulted to: play/pause, Open playlist, Stop playback.Presentation: Buttons are defaulted to: Highlighter, Pointer, Media stamp.But you can pretty much COMPLETELY customize what they do beyond that. You could reset the buttons to launch a slidehow, change slides, zoom, change volume, open a keyboard on screen, copy/paste, and more - even launching a custom application.- "Air" and Gestures. This is another area I want to spend some time on, because this is where the mouse goes from desk-bound to freedom.AIR Mode: First is just general mouse movement and interaction, with the integrated motion sensor. Basically you can move the mouse and click on things holding the mouse in the air, just like you do when it's on the desk. You push the trigger button (under the mouse) and move the mouse through the air - the cursor follows right along with you. It's not line of sight so you don't have to point it at the screen or anything. You can even hold it under the desk or across the room and it works, because it's motion sensor activated. If you plan to use it in "air" mode for a while, just double click the trigger and it will stay in that mode until you double click it again.Gestures: (which after testing out I disabled because I didn't find it useful). Gestures are when you push the central button (called the gesture button) then make a predefined sweeping motion left/right/up/down. It's basically like running a macro/command based on key press, but this is movement based (on land or air). I didn't find this especially useful but you might. Having three programmable buttons was enough, I didn't need to create yet more quick functions via a gesture. It's easy to disable with a checkbox in the settings screen.- The motion sensor is VERY good. When used in "air" mode, the mouse really does a great job of following my movements. It's not jumpy, and it smoothly moves back and forth / up and down as I rotate the mouse in the air.- Battery lasts a long time. I only charge it every few days and I've never had a problem with the battery running down. One thing that others have mentioned is that the yellow LED doesn't change to something like green when it's done charging. It doesn't, but all three do light up vs. flashing...so you do know when it's done.What just is...(these don't bother me, but your mileage may vary)- The charging station is USB powered. Using this mouse will require TWO open USB ports. First port is for the micro receiver for the mouse; Second port is for the charging station. If you have limitations on your USB ports then this could be an issue for you.What bothers me?- I keep accidentally hitting the first customizeable button and launching my web browser when I don't want to. This is mostly because of how I hold the mouse, and that the custom buttons are right on top of the device. Since I'm right handed and do a lot of clicking, my finger often pushes down enough onto the first button that it activates its custom function. This is a learning curve for me - I have to make sure I watch where my finger is, but this could be a problem for this mouse.And seriously, that's the only thing I've found so far that bothers me.Overall it's a great device that has replaced my old tethered mouse. If you do a lot of on screen presentations, or just want to control the cursor from across the room (great for a media PC in your living room), then having the "air" features is something you'll really enjoy.Have fun!

I have 3 computers, 1 media player, 1 media server and 1 wireless extender, all together sharing a broadband connection. True, the router is very outdated by today's standards (think wifi range and speed), but the fact that I still use it --- if only for routing and handling load --- tells how dependable the box is. You "set and forget", no checking, no rebooting, nothing. The fame is due.I bought other routers, and some with the same or similar platform (Buffalo WHR-HP-G54), but they were not as stable as this one. No wonder those always find a way being just an AP, while the WRT keeps routing and doing the hard work.- Features:Granted, I have a 3rd party firmware on it (have used OpenWrt and DD-WRT, now on Tomato), but that's what is good about it. QoS, "access restriction" (on/off schedule for wifi), dynamic DNS, time server or any other custom task (if you have the Linux skills) you can imagine. People run everything on them. What I do here is just the "surface" of what can be "scratched".- Cons:The outdated specs. No N, of course, range and speed seems to be on the bad side.- Support:Years ago, when I didn't know about 3rd party firmwares (that was 2005), I was having a problem with dropped Internet connection. The Linksys support on the web was quick and solved the problem (config). Mind you, after that I never used the support again, so I don't know if Linksys support is still good (or if it ever was and I was just lucky). Not knowing is, of course, a good thing in this case, and speaks favorably for the router.- Final thoughts:That's about it. Buying many things that promise more and deliver less, I'm rarely enthusiastic with electronics, but this one is a winner. Also, not trying other firmwares on this does not do it justice. Installing a 3rd party firmware is also much easier than it used to be, so anyone with reasonable knowledge and the ability to read instructions exactly as written can do it. I didn't search much lately, so I don't think if we have a comparable, proven and trusted 11n kit like the WRT was with 11g.I give it 5 stars, period. No footnotes, no asterisks, no nonsense.

Very easy to access.4) Doesn't make the rear-facing camera malfunction like most other magnetic cases.CONS:1) Doesn't work with the rear-facing camera; you have to slide the case down, which doesn't really work. $reviewer.NAME.: Randy Wakeman "Randy Wakeman"

$review_text.: The Panasonic DMC-LX7: Its Own Class of CameraThe notion of compact and "pocketable" form factor cameras is a matter of perspective. Just like an "affordable" camera has a lot to do with what you personally feel is an appropriate price bracket, if a camera is pocketable or not depends on how big your pockets are. The Lumix LX7 retails for about $500, is one of the flagship fixed lens cameras from Panasonic, yet has already been discounted in various spots to forty percent less than retail. At $300 street price, it is less dollars than some small-sensor long zoom cameras, yet is still about double the price of some very competent point and shoot cameras. If you are interested in optional (but pricey) features, the hot shoe of the LX-7 lets you instantly add the Panasonic DMW-LVF2 1,440,000-dot equivalent electronic viewfinder (about $200) or your choice of a few external flash units as well.The LX-7 is the latest incarnation of the LX-3 / LX-5 series of more or less compact cameras that have featured a bit larger sensors and brighter lenses than the run of the mill compact cameras, along with the ability to save images in RAW format. Compared to its well-received predecessor, the LX-5 has a sharper 3-inch LCD with 920,000 dots, a faster F1.4-2.3, 3.8X lens, faster shooting performance, and comparatively spectacular video capability. It records at up to Full HD video at 1080/60p and additionally offers high speed 720p video recording at 120 frames/second. Compared to the LX-5 this is a substantial upgrade, as far as I'm concerned, in most all key areas. Its CIPA standard battery life is reduced to 330 images from 400 in the LX-5, likely due to its improved resolution LCD. It is a bit heavy (0.66 lb / 10.51 oz.) and bulky (4.37 x 2.68 x 1.81 in.) compared to the shirt pocket type cameras, but similar to the LX5. It does fits the platform of pocket camera, but a coat-pocket camera rather than a shirt or pants pocket camera.LX7 Basic SpecificationsResolution: 10.10 MegapixelsLens: 3.80x zoom (24-90mm eq.)Viewfinder: LCD 920kLCD Size: 3.0 inchISO: 80-12800Shutter: 250-1/4000Max Aperture: 1.4Dimensions: 4.4 x 2.6 x 1.8 in. (111 x 67 x 46 mm)Weight: 10.5 oz (297 g) incl. batteryMSRP: $500100% crop image quality at ISO 1600 betters the upscale long zoom cameras, such as the generally impressive DMC-FZ200. Its faster lens and slightly larger sensor (1/1.7 inch) combine to make this came a low-light superstar, bettering the similar sensor size equipped Canon S100 and S110.Let's say you are considering moving up to the LX7 from a compact long zoom travel camera, such my current favorite in that class, the Lumix ZS-15 or the generally excellent Canon SX260. Now, you net the sharper LCD, a bigger sensor, and the LX7 lens is far, far faster than the ZS-15's F3.3 - F5.9 array. You'll also appreciate the included external charger, the hot shoe of the LX-7, and the obvious superior low-light capabilities. By low light, I mean the indoors version of low-light, without using the flash. If you accustomed to post-processing, the RAW images of the LX7 will be another appreciated advantage.On the flipside, the LX-7 is around twice the price, you might miss the 16x optical zoom, and you'll notice right away that the LX-7 is noticeably bigger and heavier by comparison. You'll also notice right away that there is no integral lens cover on the LX7 and the lens cap is removed manually (an aftermarket solution is readily available). If your focus (pun int.) is primarily on convenience and economy, the ZS-15 is most assuredly easier to have with you all the time, easier to quickly just throw into a pocket and go.The reasons there is so little consensus in the preferred camera is that we all have divergent notions of what a camera is supposed to do. Naturally, image quality defines a desirable camera, but there is the snapshot level of quality image and then the "I want to make posters" level. Satisfying snapshots are the most common output of a camera to no one's great surprise. Yet, if your camera has wondrous image quality, but turtle-slow shooting performance, it is easy to forego image softness only discernible if you hold an 8 x 10 a few inches from your nose in favor of a faster camera that is less hassle to use.Video capabilities get better and better in "still cameras," one of those things not important to you . . .  unless of course it is. This camera delivers strongly in the video department. The same goes with time lapse, high-speed video, creative effects, and so forth. The technically "best" image-capturing unit may not at all be the best choice for you if the image stabilization is poor, you can't see the LCD, the batteries are perpetually dead, and some of the specialty features you really want don't exist. In all of these areas, the LX-7 is either very good to class-leading.The LX-7 aspect ratio selector means you can shoot 3:2 images at 9.5 Megapixels. That completely fills the 3:2 aspect ratio screen and is where I've found myself doing most of my shooting. The image stabilization is excellent, the Panasonic "iA" (intelligent auto mode) yields impressive results if you aren't inclined to experiment with the program or scene modes.CONCLUSIONThis camera reads like a compilation of everything most people claim they want improved from their economy, compact, point and shoot. It has a better LCD, a bigger sensor, first-rate video capabilities, a hot shoe, JPEG, JPEG+RAW, and RAW capability, and includes the fastest lens in this category of camera today: F1.4-2.3. It includes an external charger as opposed to "USB only" charging, its 330 CIPA battery life is better than most compacts, and it has enough manual controls and scene modes to keep people experimenting for a very, very long time. This unit captures truly excellent video with a wondrous high speed video mode as well, 720p @ 120 fps.Time lapse, high speed video, an external charger, and a built-in neutral density filter might seem old hat by now, but it actually is ***anything but***. The next step up the food chain, the larger sensored $650 Sony Cyber-Shot DSC-RX100 lacks not just one or two of these features: it lacks all of them. Yet, the RX100 is lighter in weight, if not on the wallet, something than cannot be said for some others in the category. The RX100 actually offers very little over this camera, its diminutive size and higher resolution are the two areas that cannot be denied. What closes the gap is the extremely fast lens of the LX-7.It is hard to fault this camera. In many ways, this is a one-stop compact personal imaging center for both still images and video. The only video consideration is not the video quality, but the inability to plug in an external mic. The only thing you might miss as a still camera is the lack of a long optical zoom if you feel that cramps your personal creative juices. The overall speedy focus and shooting performance is immensely satisfying; as you won't find yourself waiting for this camera to respond. If there is such thing as a bullseye in the price / performance ratio, this camera seems to nail it.In somewhat of rare and pleasant happenstance, this camera does everything it promises to do. Not everything always works as described, but the Panasonic DMC-LX7 actually does. Those looking to upgrade from the LX5 won't have to go past the faster lens, sharper LCD, and vastly improved video to find the LX7 an appealing successor. This is simply an all-around excellent piece of equipment.It scores top-of-chart in image quality and video quality in its class. Its shooting performance makes many cameras seem turtle-slow shot-to-shot. Finally, can be considered a screamingly strong value as well. Nothing competes with it at a $300 street price that I'm aware of and I mean ***nothing***. For many, many folks this is the only camera you'll need or want . . . and it leaves scant little lacking in a non-system reasonably compact package beyond what comes in the box.I did addProgo DMW-BCJ13e Power Pack (Two Li-Ion Rechargeable Batteries and Pocket Travel AC/DC Wall Charger with Car Adapter & US to European plug) for Panasonic DMW-BCJ13, DMW-BCJ13E, DMW-BCJ13PP. Works with Lumix DMC-LX5, DMC-LX7 Digital Camera. Fully Compati...that is really quite a bargain in battery-land, and aLowepro Rezo 50 Camera Bag. The Lowepro Rezo 50 works particularly well if you go with a standard lanyard on the side of the camera rather than the dual strap supplied array. My final addition was theAuto Lens Cap for PANASONIC LUMIX DMC LX7 LX-7, LEICA D-LUX 6 + MagicFiber Microfiber Lens Cleaning Cloth.The Progo batteries are excellent, no loss of functionality vs. OEM batteries, slightly better life, and a fraction of the rip-off priced Panasonic branded batteries. With the Auto lens cap, everything goes neatly into the Rezo 50 bag including the two extra batteries. This is where it reaches, but does not exceed, my own personal limit of an easily portable camera array.Copyright 2012 by Randy Wakeman.All Rights Reserved.If you are on a budget, and want a better than standard compact camera that is a bit smaller, consider:Canon PowerShot S100 12.1 MP Digital Camera with 5x Wide-Angle Optical Image Stabilized Zoom (Black)for $249. Poor video compared to the LX7, a slower lens, weak low-light ability, but significantly smaller in size.For longer zoom, economical compacts thePanasonic LUMIX DMC-ZS15 12.1 MP High Sensitivity MOS Digital Camera with 16x Optical Zoom (Black)is a screaming deal at $149 and theCanon PowerShot SX260 HS 12.1 MP CMOS Digital Camera with 20x Image Stabilized Zoom 25mm Wide-Angle Lens and 1080p Full-HD Video (Black)is now (finally) at a competitive $200 price point.If you want a RAW capable long zoom fixed lens camera,Panasonic Lumix DMC-FZ200 12.1 MP Digital Camera with CMOS Sensor and 24x Optical Zoom - Blackis a top choice, but still at a salty $500 price point, and it is too bulky to be considered compact by most.For image quality, though, this LX-7 betters them all, and in low light or for video, it makes them all looks embarrassingly weak.

$REVIEW.: I just installed this ssd yesterday and I am loving it's performance. I upgraded from a 60gb OCZ Agility 2 and that was also a fast, worthwhile product. The reason for my upgrade is that I wanted the ability to comfortably dual-boot Win. 7 & Linux Mint 10 without having to constantly move programs and media around. I took my time with the partitioning and did plenty of research to assure proper alignment, which turned out to be fairly easy w/ Win. 7 (It automatically senses and adjusts for SSDs during install). The resulting performance is very impressive and yields me a 7.8 for primary hard disk performance in WEI. Things are even quicker w/ Linux and I simply have never used another computer with the same level of tactile speed and response. I was considering just buying another 60gb Agility 2 to run in RAID 0, but I elected to go the single, high quality drive route for stability sake. This drive also feels a bit quicker and gives me plenty of space, as I it loaded w/ Win.7 OS & speed sensitive applications on one partition (~95gb) and Linux /boot and / on the other (~15gb). My Win. 7 User files and non-speed sensitive programs are on a 465gb partition of a Caviar Black 1tb HDD with the remaining 465gb partitioned for swap and /home for Linux Mint. All of my movies, music, and backups are on another Caviar Black 1tb formatted to a single NTFS partition. Gparted running off a Linux live disc turned out to be a great tool for partitioning all of the drives after the initial offset and partition was done by the Win. 7 advanced drive options utility on the install disk. Time will tell if this drive holds up well, but the features (SandForce controler & TRIM) seem to indicate I will get great use out of it. Additionally, from what I understand, OCZ has done a nice job of providing firmware updates, though they lack a comprehensive utility for monitoring the drive. I love this drive and I have found adding an SSD to be one of the single most effective upgrades, in terms of speed, that one could make to a computer. I would buy another one of these drives if my finances allowed. GREAT PRODUCT!

$REVIEW.: I feel that this kit is a definite must buy when buying the Freestyle keyboard.  With a split keyboard design, unless you buy 2 mouse sized rests, you're going to have a hard time finding wristrests that properly support your hands.  And proper hand support means supporting the heel of your hand, not your wrists themselves.  Putting pressure on your wrists will put pressure on the carpal tunnel and will actually aggravate the tendons and nerves in the tunnel, making your symptoms worse.  You want to support the heel of your hand on the squishy part.  This kit does a good job of that w/ built in wrist supports and a stick on soft layer.I do have some issues with the kit though.First off, it's way expensive for what it is.  I feel like it should be $25 or so.  It's just a prop-up kit, and wrist rests made of plastic.  But I understand that they probably don't move as much inventory as Microsoft and other companies, thus the price.Another issue is that the stick on soft layer is sort of like a neoprene layer, so I imagine it'll get dirty, and probably harbor lots of bacteria if you have sweaty hands.  I don't have sweaty hands, so it's not much of an issue, but I can imagine it getting pretty funky if you do.  I think it would've been better to have a non-porous soft material that could be cleaned by wiping it off.The feet on this kit aren't very grippy either, so the keyboard has a tendency to move day to day.  Not too big of an issue, but for the price, it should grip better.All in all, I think the keyboard needs this kit with it, but I gave it 4 stars because of the stuff mentioned above.

$Helpful?.: [0, 0] $review_date.: 05 25, 2014
$review_text.: I got this NAS because I wanted something I could back up a few files to and serve my movie collection to my PCs and Raspberry Pis running XBMC

I was torn between a consumer solution like this and a prosumer from Synloogy

I opted to go for this because I found one for $170, roughly the cost of the hard drive itself
This way I could just open up the NAS and just use the bare hard drive and I wouldn't be out any money if the My Cloud ended up sucking
I don't think I'll be doing that, because I've been pleasantly surprised - when writing to the NAS, I got an average speed of 55 - 65mb/s (440 - 520mbps), with read speeds of 70 - 80mb/s (560 - 640mbps)
I was expecting quite a bit less from an underpowered CPU and a skimpy amount of memory, but WD really gets the most out of these limited resources
I was also impressed with the web interface

There isn't too much to actually do besides adding users and shares and performing a few maintenance tasks, but it's easy to use and very responsive

The device itself is very clean, with a gigabit Ethernet port, USB 3.0 port for backups (but not printer sharing), and power jack

 The only hitch I ran into was when I first fired it up, it didn't recognize the drive
I ended up having to do a full reset and it's been fine ever since, but it's still very strange to have to do that for a brand new product.I've had this for a day and a half, and so far I love it
Unless you're a video editor and you're copying raw, uncompressed video back and forth or something like that, the WD My Cloud will probably be fine (but if you are that heavy user, go with the a Synology NAS or the like)


It can serve very high bitrate blu ray rips just fine and backing up even a few hundred gigabytes of data only takes a little over an hour (assuming you're using a gigabit switch)

If your usage is similar to mine, go for it.

If you are in the market for an mp3 player, I strongly recommend the Clip+ as your first choice.  If you are like me and already have the iPod Nano, still consider the Clip+ to come through where the Nano falls short.

The Toshiba was an I5, which was pretty fast, but for me this time around I wanted graphics over speed. With an AMD processor you always have the option of overclocking the processor if your a techy. No matter how much I have running the laptop just still seems to run cool. Very Good!Overall....Excellent! I've been so used to 17" screens, the 15.6" is something I need to get used to but it is alot more portable.One thing that is keeping me from giving it 5 stars.....when the screen turns off there is a white shadow on the bottom right corner. I've read several complaints about this but it looks like to me its because of the HP Logo that is lite up while the laptop is on. Not sure if there is anyway to turn it off but thats whats causing the issue. Overall though its nothing to make me dislike this laptop.

$REVIEW.: Like most camera owners, we have what seems like tons of 35mm negatives boxed up hiding on the top shelf of the closet


A surprisingly good, low cost alternative to sending out those treasured negatives to be processed is the Wolverine F2D Film to Digital Scanner


Make no mistake, this product is not going to revive what time took away
What it does do is provide above average (5 mega pixels) scans of negatives/slides without downloading software or linking to a computer.Out of the box, the Wolverine F2D is outfitted with a built in 1.5" color LCD screen

Power, flip, mirror and OK/Scan buttons are located on the top of the unit


This model comes with both a film negative and slide trays


The trays holds up to six images

Both trays are mounted with an easy to close magnetic latch

A 1gb SD card, cleaning brush, USB cable, USB power adapter and users manual are all included in the box


Buyers beware, my associate purchased the same unit from a third party Amazon vendor and found that both the SD card and USB cable missing.After reading the instruction manual, I opted to power up the F2D via my computer's USB port

Remember, it can also be plugged into an AC outlet


Start up was a breeze
Just insert the SD card (card contacts facing up) until you hear a click


Press the orange power button to power up
Once I inserted the tray viewing my negatives was instant

Press the OK/Copy button to scan


Press the button again to save images to the SD card


An hour glass will appear on the screen when scanning

A blinking red dot shows up when the unit is ready for the next scan


Just slide the tray into position and the next image is ready to be scanned
I was surprised with the clarity of each image viewed via the LCD screen.For better scanning results, I recommend cleaning the scanner with the enclosed brush before inserting the next negative strip


Also spraying both the film tray and negatives/slides with canned air can sometimes make all the difference
After scanning, I uploaded the images onto my computer via the SD card
With the exception of water spotting and scratches my scanned photographs were surprisingly crisp

Instead of using Photoshop, I opted to utilize Google's Picasa 3 photo software to try and correct the imperfections
I was happy with the end result.With the exception of keeping the unit safe from dust, heat and water, maintenance on this product is a no brainer


There are no bulbs or parts to remove and replace


The light source is powered by 3 White LEDs

Besides the aforementioned enclosed tools, the Wolverine F2D Scanner comes with the standard one year limited warranty

The manufacturer provides a surprisingly responsive customer support number which is available Monday through Friday 9am-5pm PST.Contrary to older reviews, I found no real problems with the Wolverine F2D 100 Film to Digital Scanner


Paired with the right retouching software, it is a good working companion that covers the basics

It goes without saying, this model is a low cost alternative to professional photo retouching services.After a couple of issues with product quality and returns policy via third party Amazon partners/vendors, I now make every effort to ensure a safe purchase directly from Amazon

Sometimes I may pay a few more dollars, but its money well spent

If Amazon doesn't have it in stock I don't buy it from one of its partners/vendors
Amazon goes out of its way with providing outstanding customer service and a 30 day money back guarantee

That said, I do recommend this product.

$REVIEW.: How it looks: The silver version of this drive has a brushed aluminum front with rough etched Seagate logo, rest of the drive case is plastic.  It is the same silver as a macbook but since it is brushed instead of powder coated it catches a lot more light.  Not unattractive.  Thankfully the LED light is white and pulses rather than WD's annoying blue led flicker, the thin white light goes off when not used for awhile.Sizing: Compared to an iPhone 5 the Seagate Slim USB3 500GB drive is a little bit thicker (~2-3mm), shorter length wise (~1cm) and wider width wise (~2cm).Speed: This drive uses a standard blue USB 3 cable (included) that is backwards compatible to USB2 meaning that you can plug it into any Mac or PC.  Thunderbolt drives are the fastest, but this drive isn't compatible with Seagate's Thunderbolt adapter.  USB 3 is fast, but if you connect it to a Mac that doesn't have USB 3 support it will run at the very slow USB 2 speed (ie long file copy times).  Unlike PCs which use a blue USB port to indicate USB 3 compatibility a Mac doesn't easily tell you if it is USB 3 or USB 2.  You'll have to look up your model specs by going to the Apple icon, choosing about this Mac, more info and then googling your model number for details (surprising this isn't made easier, but any Mac model made earlier than mid 2012 probably doesn't have USB 3 support).It shows up in the Mac finder as &#34;Seagate Slim Drive&#34; with an Orange USB icon drive.  It contains a Mac and Windows installer and 400mb of videos (why they couldn't ship a single higher quality MPEG4 with multiple audio tracks is beyond me).  The list of files on the drive are at the bottom of this review.Drive is formatted NTFS and has no support for SMART drive sensors or hardware encryption.  If you want to optimize it for a Mac only environment or plan on using Time Machine for backups you will need to launch Disk Utility on your Mac to erase the drive.  I chose Mac OS extended (Journaled, Encrypted) because I plan on using it to backup my MacBook Air via Time Machine and don't want anyone finding my drive to be able to access the contents (uses software encryption which is slower than WD's version).  It should just take a minute to format.If you get the error message: Disk Encryption. Disk Erase failed with the error: Couldn&#8217;t unmount disk, then you should make sure to dismount the disk image (drag drive to trash) and try again.  You can't be accessing the drive while trying to format it.If you go into Time Machine's preferences you can now add the Seagate drive as a replacement or as an addition.  I use my Airport Time Capsule at home and wanted to add this drive as a backup at work so I added both.  In the time it has taken me to write this review Time Machine has backed up 7GB of the 72GB needed.  Wishing Seagate had a slim thunderbolt drive, but Apple is already onto thunderbolt 2 so I'm feeling a bit behind on this USB 2 only Mid 2011 MacBook Air!Files on the drive are:Seagate Dashboard Boy did I love my Tau :)ABOUT DELIVERY SERVICES:I purchased this television through Amazon from Electronics Expo.  They used a delivery service called Manna Distribution Services.  A single delivery man came and brought the TV into the house - a 'threshhold' delivery, just inside the door. I signed for it and off he went.  I then took the cardboard cover off the top and discovered the TV screen was shattered.  I immediately contacted Electronics Expo, who asked me to provide some pictures of the TV, which I did.  He asked if I wanted to cancel the order or a new TV, I wanted a new TV.  He took care of the arrangements.  Ten days later Manna Distrubtion Services again came, took the broken TV and delivered the new one.  Before I would sign I undid the box and had a look at the screen and this TV was in apparent good shape.  I signed and off he went.The moral of this is do not be timid about inspecting any product that is delivered to you.  For myself I am uncomfortable with doing it, but for a high cost item such as this, and the amount of time (ten days) I had to have it in my house (my house is small so this was a major imposition - and also I had no TV in the livingroom for this whole period of time), it is well worth the effort to examine the product before signing.  If broken, refuse delivery.All in all I feel Electronics Expo did a good job, as well as Manna Distribution Services regarding delivery.  I only wish I had been less timid and thoroughly examined the TV before I signed for it.  I am pointing this out for the rest of you so that you don't make the same mistake I did.SOUND:I am not rating the sound portion of this TV.  I have not even turned on the TV speakers to be honest, as I have it connected to a Marantz SR6003 a/v receiver via HDMI and listen to the sound through Acoustic Research AR1 Hi-Res speakers. You will have to connect to Logitech's Harmony website first to register before you can start programming the remote.It comes with low discharge batteries - applause! First, it is categorized vaguely as a computer media player. Then it does not have an "OK" button. It took me about 30 minutes doing research on forums and FAQs to make it work.Once you have a successfully functioning remote, try to avoid using your other remotes from now on. The Harmony works with combination of devices. Generally you only need to push one button to turn on everything that you need to turn on. If you want to watch a DVD; your DVD player, TV and receiver will turn on at the same time. It will also choose the correct input for your TV. But once you use another remote, the program sequence will be disrupted. If you go back to your Harmony, you can no longer use a single button operation and now you need some fixing. That's where to Help button comes in.The help button is very useful as it can walk you through when you encountered any problems, like when a device is off when it is supposed to be on and vice versa. $REVIEW.: Lately, I've been bringing my notebook computer to a local bookstore/cafe to do some writing. It's a cozy place but pretty noisy. The selection of music over the speakers wasn't the greatest either. I decided that I would make my own mix of MP3 music files and bring them along so I could listen to them through my headphones. Since I'm working on my notebook computer, I didn't want to run the files off of my hard drive, which would run down my battery. My solution was to load all the MP3 files on a Flash Drive - no moving parts, a much smaller drain on battery power. I purchased the SD 512 Flash drive. The following is my experience with this device:The unit itself is a pretty small device. (See product details above for size, etc) and has a total capacity of 512mb. The actual usable memory is closer to 487mb or so. This is due to the software/operating/security program that is preloaded onto the drive. I run Windows XP on my notebook, and the SanDisk booted up immediately without any problems. You can &#34;lock out&#34; anyone from viewing your files by running the security program. Be careful not to quick click through the prompts as you may miss entering the password. You can also download the latest encrption software for free. According to Sandisk, the new lock/encrption program is fourteen times more secure and is a much better program.Performance was smooth as silk. There were no drivers to install and the plug and play feature worked the very first time. I &#34;mix&#34; my MP3's on my desktop computer which runs Windows ME and transfer them on the Sandisk to my notebook which runs Windows XP. There were no problems in switching back and forth between systems. I've heard that you need to download drivers if you run Windows 98. I do not know how well this drive works under '98' but it seems to work great with ME or XP. I loaded and ran my MP3 files from the Sandisk and was able to play back my music files without a hitch. Since this is a flash drive, you can load practically any type of file you want on it, be it photo files, documents etc. I decided this particular drive would be used just for music files. There is a green light at the end of the drive which flashes rapidly whenever the drive is being used. Which brings me to the next point...If you have not used one of these devices before, it is extrememly important to *disconnect the device properly* before you physically remove it. You must first click on the &#34;remove device&#34; icon. The operating system will disconnect and will then tell you that removal is safe. If you just *unplug the device* without proper shut down procedures, sooner or later, you will most likely either fry your unit or corrupt the data. This is not a defect with the unit, you must remove all flash devices in this manner. Those of you who are familiar with the Sony Playstation know that if you pull out the memory card before it is finished saving, you will end up with corrupt data or a damaged card. The same holds true for flash disk devices.There have been reliability issues associated with this unit, but I am either a very lucky guy or the reports of failure are due to user error, i.e. unpluging the unit before shutting down properly. Perhaps their was a bad batch of them. I don't know. What I do know is that the unit has performed great, (so far), and I am very pleased with the performance and price. There are promotional discounts given my some vendors, so if you can snag one with a rebate, you'll be paying only a few dollars more for this 512mb over a 256mb.As far as the music that's loaded onto my Sandisk Cruzer, I've got a good selection of trance, new age, classical and eurodance.Just in case you wanted to know. &#60;grin&#62;
$SUMMARY.: So far, so good.

$review_text.: I've tried and owned lots of headphones, both inexpensive and costly, and I was amazed when I tried these out. The bass is rich and thick and heavy, and it hits all the high notes clearly, and they blend together without any muddle. The dual dynamic drivers (6.8 mm "woofers" & 9mm "tweeters") hit all the notes, and unlike many other in-ear phones I've tried, it doesn't feel like the sounds lay on top of one another, but they are articulated, expansive, and clear. This is true, whether I'm listening to hip-hop, alternative, electronic, jazz, or classical.If you go from a standard pair of headphones -- say the kind they give you when you buy a new phone -- and try these you'll be astonished by how much better your music can sound. If you go from these to, say, a much more expensive pair of in-ear phones billed as audiophile quality, you may not be able to tell the difference. For the price, these are hands down the best value best sounding headphones I've tried. (I was offered a chance to try these out by the manufacturer, for the purpose of testing and review.)In addition to sound quality the build feels solid, and looks good. The earpieces are made of a solid two tone plastic (deep dark red and black). The cable (1.2 m = roughly 4 feet) doesn't deliver any noise or interference that I can detect. The plug is a standard 3.5mm gold plated jack, and it comes with a 1/4" adapter as well as one of the two-pronged airplane adapters. You also get several extra silicone tips and a foam tip for extra insulation against external noise. As with most Brainwavz headphones, this also comes with a hard-shell case that you can use to keep the headphones from getting banged up, and also to store the additional plugs and spare earpieces.One thing I was happily surprised by is that the earphone shape -- which consists of a flattened egg shaped base, from which the earplugs extend -- does a much better job securing these in place in my ear than any in-ear phone I've tried. I think that the design is primarily there to house the dual drivers, responsible for the deeper range of sound. Still, it serves a secondary purpose of fitting my ears perfectly. I can run with these in and they don't even wobble.These are a great value pair of earphones that deliver audiophile quality sound for a fraction of the cost. They offer an astonishing and easily noticeable improvement on the kind of standard low range earphones that I used to buy before I'd realized how much better it can get.One last thing: they come in a very handsome package, and would make an ideal gift for anyone who likes to listen to music. That's nice for when I throw them into my bag, or even in my pocket so I can have them ready for when I want to plug them into my phone or laptop and enjoy the sounds.

$Helpful?.: [27, 28] $review_date.: 04 28, 2010
$REVIEW.: Doing this review was a little difficult because the basic functionality of most external hard drives is the same, which is storing and backing up data from one or multiple computers
 External hard drives have become a commodity, so you need to think about what makes this drive different and what factors make an external hard drive better or worse

 The answer will typically depend on these factors:1) how much data do you need to store on the external drive?2) how often and in what quantities do you add or remove data?3) do you need to access the data over a home or work network or will you connect the external hard drive to your home or laptop computer?I own three external hard drives


 Two are USB (including this model) and one is eSATA


 If you are frequently transferring large quantities of data then you should buy an eSATA external hard drive because the data transfer speed is at least 5x faster than USB
 For example, I can copy/paste 40,000 photos and 2,000 MP3s at a blistering rate with eSATA
 I can still perform the same procedure with USB but it will take longer

 If you are not in a big rush, then don't bother with eSATA..


the USB will work fine.PROS- very easy to use- quiet- smallCONS- none notedCOMPARING (to other related devices)- Not as fast as eSATA, but this point is irrelevant if you don't need to have the faster transfer speeds.- Not a NAS (Network Attached Storage) which simply means an external hard drive with expanded functionality
 This feature is really cool if you want todump all of your media (songs, pictures) and hook the external hard drive up to a wireless router
 NAS allows for file sharing and storage over a network.Bottom line: this hard drive does a terrific job for what it is designed to do: storage and backup.NOTE: an eSATA hard drive requires an eSATA connection on your computer


 I had to buy an eSATA card for my home computer ($20 at local electronics store) so I could use my eSATA drive.

$Helpful?.: [0, 0] $reviewDate.: 09 10, 2013
$REVIEW.: When I first purchased my iPad Mini, I spent days surfing case options and debating what I wanted.  For my phone, I'm a longtime devotee of Otterbox Defenders...which have saved my having to replace many a dropped phone...but I wasn't sure that I wanted something that bulky for the Mini.  I ended up with a Speck Candyshell grip, which is a very nice case when holding / using the Mini, but which left me needing additional protection for it before I could toss it in my bag, since the screen was unprotected.  The Airbender Mini was an attractive alternative, offering protection similar to that of the Defender with the added benefit of a bluetooth keyboard.  Having tried it out, I have to say, I'm very impressed.Things I like:- Case design - 2-layer protection, similar to the Otterbox; very nice coverage of all buttons/access points to the device, keeping everything fully accessible but keeping them well protected; nice materials, solid feel (without adding too much weight).  It's not the easiest thing to get on, but I can't quibble with the end result, and in the grand scheme of things, it's far from the most challenging case I've tried to get an electronic device into.  It's also a very nice looking case, both when separated from the keyboard and when combined as a clamshell.- The case mount arm - easy snap on/snap off ability to attach/release the case to the arm.  Arm secures into the keyboard to create a clamshell arrangement, but also slides out so that you have a free-standing stand to hold the Mini separate from the keyboard- Keyboard bluetooth pairing was quick and easy- Keyboard quick button controls to iPad functionality are very convenient- Good keyboard battery life, good charge time of keyboard battery- Keys are very responsive, and I like the chicklet design/feel- Powers the screen on when I open the clamshellThings I would like to see improved:- While I like the free-standing stand, it feels less than stable, and depending on the angle that you set the device at, can topple over.  It takes a little getting used to- While I like that the stand slides out, I'd like a &#34;stop&#34; that keeps me from sliding it fully out when I don't intend to.  It's a minor annoyance, but still an annoyance when your one-piece case is suddenly two pieces when it's not what you intendedThe keys are (naturally, given the size of the Mini) smaller than standard, as is the spacing, so this is not a keyboard that I think I could ever touch type on.  That's not specific to this keyboard - I have never been able to &#34;adjust&#34; mentally to a smaller than standard keyboard, which is my personal failing, since I know others are able to.  Since it's not specific to this keyboard, I don't consider it a pro or con of the keyboard itself, but still worth mentioning - if you're someone who struggles with small keyboards...this is a small keyboard (it's a Mini, for heaven's sake!!).  This is not a keyboard that I would attempt to type war and peace on...but no keyboard that is sized comparable to the Mini would be.  Given the size constraints, this keyboard significantly increases my ability to do quick, short entries into my Mini, while offering an easy way to disengage from the keyboard and simply have a nice, protective case in settings in which I don't anticipate any need for typing.

$reviewerName.: Cannon
$Helpful?.: [178, 187] $review_date.: 10 12, 2010
$review_text.: In world where tracking the awesomeness of your run seem to be more and more imperative - actually, I don't even know what that means.The Nike + technology includes this little device that fits in a little hollowed out area beneath the insert of your favorite Nike shoe.  The device is essentially a pedometer that is pretty darn accurate.  It transmits information to either a Nike armband/wrist band or an iPod nano and helps runners or walkers track their distance, time, and speed.First, you won't feel the device in your shoe.  I read a review on another website in which a nice lady was complaining bitterly about how she could feel it in her shoe.  Chances are, she failed to remove the little foam patch that currently occupies the little area where the Nike + sensor is supposed to go.  Once removed, the sensor will fit in that hole and is flush with the bottom of the inside of the shoe.  Once you put the insert back in over the sensor, you'll never know it's there.  I also read someone else indicate that they could feel a weight difference once it was in the shoe.  This is, in a word, absurd.  If your body is so finely tuned that you can detect a weight difference between the shoe with the device and the shoe without it, you are truly an amazing human being, and I suspect you have x-ray vision and can run faster than a speeding bullet.The reason the product gets 4 stars and not 5 is this:  The website is less than impressive.  The sensor transmits information to your wristband or iPod and can then be used to track your performance on Nike's website.  It's nice that you can do this.  The device comes, right out of the box, essentially "accurate" for the average runner, but it can be fine tuned for those that want even more accurate results.  Where the website fails though, is its inability to provide some fairly basic information about a run.  It can tell you your pace at a number of graphed points on your run, but it doesn't tell you - and this is really sort of nuts - how fast you ran each mile.  Rather, when you click on the point on the graph at each mile marker, it tells you your pace at that moment in your run.There are alternative websites that apparently can provide the "rest of the story" and give you the information you are seeking, and a simple internet search will provide you with their names.... but it is rather odd that Nike hasn't fixed this aspect of the site.The Nike+ community is, overall, very supportive and pleasant.  The site is useful to track your runs, set goals, participate in challenges, etc.I've compared the accuracy to a gps running watch and I believe that the accuracy is essentially the same.  I found that I could access some of the information on the gps watch a little easuer than Nike + but, I found the gps watch to be a bit bulky.  I do like how with Nike Plus, you have the option of wearing a wrist band or an iPod Nano, in your pocket or strapped to your arm.  This allows users to select an option that is best for their comfort.  There are adaptors available that will allow you to use Nike + with other shoe brands.  I have NOT tested those.Another helpful tip.... Nike has finally gotten with the program and made running shoes in a variety of widths.  Accordingly, if you, like me, could "never own a pair of Nike running shoes" because they were "too narrow and I have Fred Flinstone feet" take another look.  Now that shoes come in different widths, you will be pleasantly surprised.  This means the Nike + technology can appeal to a wider clientele - like those of us that are not built like sleek, running machines.One final note.... I took the Nike + on a hike and found that in steep sections, the device could not be accurrate.  This is because you must move at a certain pace with a reasonable stride for the device to work.  When hiking a mountain, you often take short steps and move slower than the device can record (or, coming down, longer strides, etc) so don't expect the device to accurately capture that kind of a hike.  As for gps technology on mountain hikes, it's a mixed bag by the time you factor in tree cover, pace, stride, etc.  Just FYI.I recommend Nike +  I use it, and I like it, and I've been using it for about 5 months now.  As a beginning runner, it's accurate enough for me, it's motivating, in a sense, and well worth the investment.  With website improvements, this is a 5 star device.If you have questions, post them in the comment section and I'll answer....  Thanks.

$product.ID.: B00D5Q75RC
$reviewer.NAME.: kaimbanks
$Helpful?.: [4, 4] $review_date.: 05 26, 2014
$review_text.: I purchased this speaker recently to use it at a number of small gatherings / parties as the end of my senior year of high school approaches. I chose it over other similarly-priced competitors based off of its looks, overall reputation for sounding great, and name-brand backing.Long story short, it deserves the hype that it gets from pretty much every major electronics reviewer out there. It's built amazingly well, sounds unbelievable for such a tiny little speaker, and is loud enough for outdoor gatherings. Here's a brief list of pros and cons that I've encountered over my 2 or 3 weeks of usage:PROS:- Great sound quality (great bass, VERY crisp mid and upper levels, never distorts at higher volumes)- Loud (loud enough to easily fill a bedroom/dorm room with uncomfortably loud sound, also loud enough to suffice as a sound source for outdoor pool parties / gatherings)- Great battery life (I used it once for a 5-hour outdoor party and there was no perceptible drop in volume or sound quality)- Long range (works great outdoors - 30+ foot Bluetooth range, and the sound quality doesn't drop within its range)- Can pair with lots of devices (I use an iPad, HTC One, MacBook Pro, and Xbox with bluetooth transceiver)- Nice charging station is included and can be used as a dock even while the speaker is playingCONS:- Pricey- HEAVY. You do not expect this speaker to weigh as much as it does. Not a problem for me, because I don't mind lugging around a heavy backpack, but it still has quite a bit of heft.- No &#34;easy&#34; way to switch between Bluetooth inputs. I often switch between my HTC and MacBook, which involves pressing the little bluetooth button on the speaker and manually connecting it on my desired device, which is a little cumbersome. Thankfully it only requires about 10 seconds of fuddling to get it to work.Things to note, neither bad nor good:- Some people claim that the speaker's bass sounds better when it's several inches from a wall. I don't disagree, but it's often a little tricky to find the optimal distance when you're in a hurry to get the music going for a party.- Can't be charged by Micro-USB. This wasn't a problem for me, because the battery life is easily good enough for my uses and I just set it on the dock at night, but for VERY mobile users this could be a bit troublesome.I can heartily recommend this speaker to just about anyone. It works perfectly for my requirements - bedroom listening to classical music and top Spotify charts, and outdoor party music - and sounds great to me even though I'm very picky about my sound equipment. I would NOT purchase this speaker if you need something ultra-portable because it's so heavy (one of Logitech's tiny speakers might serve you better), but for anybody else, this thing is flawless. There's a reason it's the #1 seller for Bluetooth speakers right now on Amazon. Enjoy!
$review_summary.: Excellent little speaker! Perfect for gatherings/bedroom use
